In article <3mmrr3$7tu@nic.umass.edu>, SYFRIED@frost.oit.umass.edu (Sy
Friedman) wrote:

> I just recieved teh new rules and was suprised that no generation rules for
> standard humans were present.  I own these rules separately from the "solo"
> adventures, but they should have been included.  So far what little I have
> browsed seems to be nicely done.  The artwork is pleasant, and volume 3 is of
> great use in running a game.  The first two volumes reprint much of S&G volume
> 2, while these are somewhat clearer I was hoping for more.  Also no non/semi
> intelligent beasties included in rules, although I again have the Bestiary. 
> This is not as important as character rules which really should have been
> included.  I know TOME is a business, and they already have these rules out,
> but a stripped down version could have easily been included.  The map is very
> nice, as are all the maps ever printed for Tekumel games.  I do like the
> archetypes and their illustrations.  A little bit
> of background and an index would also have been nice. As it stands it is quite
> nice for those of us who already own previous materials, but lack too much for
> those interested in it as a new game.
> 
> 
> Seth Friedman 

Thanks for the comments. I, too, wish that we could have included the
character generation rules AND the Bestiary in this boxed set, but many
players have the separately published versions already, and they would no
doubt have screamed at the extra price needed to print and box these
previously printed items along with the rules. At today's publishing
costs, it would have added $40-$50 to the price. The box was always
intended to contain just the RULES for roleplaying. The beginner does get
the beautifully drawn archetypes, and thus have some characters with
backgrounds and stats to start off with. The advanced player will already
own the first "Adventures on Tekumel" book, which provides the character
generation system, as well as the Bestiary. These new rules will fill in a
major gap for him/her. The truly advanced player will want the nonhuman
stat-generating rules included in the new rules set but will have all the
other stuff, including "Ebon Bindings," "Deeds of the ever Glorious," the
old Zocchi Sourcebook, etc. There is just no way to get these things ALL
into one box! This should not really bother people used to separate
"monster books," "gods and goddesses books," etc. etc. I owned a veritable
stack of such game-aids and modules when I first started to roleplay.
Other games have developed "world books" to describe a single planet (with
one domindant species), a region, a single civilisation, a single mythos,
etc. Tekumel is so big and contains so many different cultures, species,
and features that ONE "world book" would e har put to do the job. The old
Sourcebook covered the societies of northern Tekumel, but it didn't
include the "monsters"; the Bestiary fills that role but doesn't go into
much detail about the intelligent nonhumans' cultures. I still want to do
a "city" book so that people can see how a major Tekumelani city operates
and can find their way around the Imperial bureaucracies with some ease.

I think that beginners will indeed have a tough time with Tekumel. They
always have. NO set of rules can include enough to make the planet
familiar to newcomers. Remember that most sword-and-sorcery fantasy
roleplaying rules are based on familiar (to Americans) images: dragons,
castles, knights, ape-like critters, lions and tigers and bears...! I
remember that even vampires in tuxedoes were once included in one popular
"monster" list. We all instantly recognise the comicbook,
Saturday-afternoon-matinee, TV-series-beasts, but nobody knows what an
Ahoggya is, or a Pe Choi, or a Dlaqo. In the first "Empire of the Petal
Throne" I offered two or three line descriptions of the "critters," but
this caused more complaints than I had ever imagined: people were not
satisfied with such short introductions to a wholly unfamiliar "monster"
or alien race. Hence, the Bestiary. The character generation book came
about for similar reasons: it's easy to present dice rolls for the usual
statistics: "strength," "build," etc., but this does not present these
"stats" in any meaningful societal context. Tekumel's societies are very
different from those familiar to North Americans. So I developed the
character roll-up book, which has societal materials and "background"
included along with the "stats." I then added solo adventures which
present still more background: how the armies, temples, and clans work,
how shopping is done, how to travel, how the countryside looks, etc. etc.
Characters developed during these "adventures" can be introduced into any
roleplaying game, replete with background, possessions, interests, and
experience. I didn't want the rules themselves to be incomplete, however,
and so I devised the archetypes as a compromise: pre-rolled characters
>from  a variety of backgrounds and with a variety of skills. They are
enough for the beginner -- and probably enough also for the intermediate
player. As I said above,the advanced player may want to roll up a
character from scratch and will require the white book. This should be no
big obstacle: many games require the use of books other than the central
rulebook. All in all, the Tekumel "set" is still somewhat cheaper than
those of certain other major games.

TOME is a small company and is pressed for cash.There won't be any more
Tekumel materials unless this game makes money. Sorry, but those are the
economic facts. Shortcuts have to be taken, but I still think players are
getting their money's worth, at least in today's inflated market.

I'm glad you like the map. Please send copies of your letters to TOME so
that they are apprised of your needs, likes, and dislikes. I am sure they
will do whatever they can.

-- 
M. A. R. Barker

> Fungi and Religion
> Certain religions, in particular the temples of Sarku and Durritlamish, view
> even be cultivated, harvested, and sold fresh or dried and exported.
> fungi as sacred food. They spring from dead things, so must be a gift of the
> God of death and undeath. These fungi might be consumed in rituals, some of
> which might contribute to religious visions. They could also be cultivated
> in the underworlds and consumed as delicacies or common food.

Yes, fungi are a common food source, particularly in the great rainforests
of Pan Chaka. The Pachi Lei make much use of several species. Others are
poisonous or emit dangerous spores. Sarku's worshippers cultivate a
particular black fungus for food, Dried, this is used as an amulet to ward
off various animals.

> I feel that the temples of Hru'u and Ksarul would also favor the consumption
> of fungi, and might even purchase hallucinogenic varieties from the Sarku and
> Durrit temples. They would not view it as such a holy food, however. The
> temples of Belkhanu and Qon might also favor these foods.

I don't recall hallucinogenic fungi being used by the temples of Ksarul
and Hru'u, but then, I was never one for pharmacology. It's quite
possible. Belkhanu and Qon do not prefer fungi but make no rules against
them. There are special fungi named for Belkhanu, for Qon (the "Risen
Lord," which is small, pallid white with yellow markings, and is deadly to
small animals, children, etc. but not to adult humans -- it is said to
taste like creamy pudding and to cause delightful dreams).

> I see the temples of Vimuhla and Chiteng as completely eschewing fungi, as the
> spawn of Sarku and his servant Missum.

You are correct. Vimuhla, Chiteng, Karakan, Chegarra, and Dilinala argue
that fungi are "of the dark" and should not be eaten, although there is no
total prohibition. They can be consumed in times of starvation.

I am not sure what doctrinal opinion might be held by worshippers of
Avanthe and Dilinala, although I am of the opinion that Avanthe temples
would take no particular position. Most other temples would take no
interest in this question.

Avanthe treats fungi as part of the natural cycle of life/death, and as
long as these parasites are not connected directly with the Dark Gods, She
has no problems with them. 

 
> Where to Find Fungi
> Just like on earth, fungus grow better in damp, cool conditions. Thus, the
> underworlds would be outstanding locations for growth of fungi. Certain
> locales would also breed fungi well, such as around Purdimal, where the
> variety of different types would be staggering. In some of these are type may
> even be cultivated, harvested, and sold fresh or dried and exported.

Absoutely correct. Try Penom, though, for really horrendous fungi -- some
semi-sentient, some as tall as a house! The things grow in a riot of
colours, textures, and shapes. They coat the walls of underworld corridors
and cannot be touched without giving off deadly spores. Avoid them when
you can.

> Uses of Fungi
> Fungal growths may be used for food, to make drugs, and in religious services
> as mentioned above. Some types, found only in the deepest underworlds or in
> the furthest reaches of the barbarian mountains, may sell as delicacies for
> hundreds of kaitars for a single gram. Especially those that not only taste
> good, but impart "altered reality" to the eater. Other varieties may be ground
> into powders and used as spices or consumed as drugs for medicinal or
> recreational purposes.

Right, although I never heard of any costing hundreds of Kaitars per gram
for food! Hallucinogenic fungi probably are sold for high prices, of
course.
>  
> Appearances of Fungi
> Tekumelyani fungi are at least as diverse as those found on earth. An edible
> mushroom particularly favored by Sarku worshippers and found only in the
> underworld is known as the Deathhead, because it vaguely resembles as
> small human skull. Another, the Scepter of Belkhanu, appears as a long staff
> topped by a small golden knob. (How the hell did you know about this?)

If you want to see pure viscera-twisting ugliness, get one of the
experienced fungus-harvesters of Penom to bring up one of the fungi called
the Dark King's Crown. The smell and sight cause even hardened warriors to
lose their lunch.
>  
> Just some initial thoughts on an admittedly odd topic.
> Any additional thoughts or comments are welcome and encouraged. Maybe I'll
> experiment with some recipes and post those as well.

Ugh... I happen to love mushrooms, but I wouldn't fool with Tekumelani
fungi unless I had a convenient food-taster.

-- 
M. A. R. Barker

On Fri, 7 Apr 1995, Anton Dovydaitis wrote:
> Barker's world is a superior product: the vision usually reserved for
> a literary figure, combined with the intellectual rigor of a social
> scientist.  So why hasn't it been more successful in the market?
> 
	I agree on this.  It's only been the mismanagement of the 
previous companies in getting the goods to the public.  Every company 
after TSR has mishandled Tekumel, treating it as if it were some kinky 
sex thing, to be treated as quietly and under-the-table as possible.
	That is, until TOME stepped into the picture.  Here, I know they 
lack the funds for advertising, but I wish they'd go ahead and sink the 
money into promoting a product they've worked so hard to produce....

 
> But it seems to me that an essentially iconoclastic rules systems is
> counter-productive media to market Tekumel, whose best appeal is 
> its total vision.  Roleplaying has evolved to the point where the
> best rules DON'T get in the way.  While Barker often exhorts the
> utility of on-the-fly refereeing, his published rules sets to date
> are too cumbersome to be appealing to the current generation of
> roleplayers, and this serves to impede market adaption.
>

	In a time where all role-playing is suffering at the hands of 
card games, this is not really a valid point.  Each RPG has to have its 
own gimmick to sell it, otherwise, people are going to say, "What!?  
ANOTHER RPG?  *YAWN!*"
	 Just like rock groups have to keep coming up with newer and 
weirder/stupider acts to attract fans, so do RPG's have to have their own 
uniqueness to compete with the card game craze.


> Instead, it is the WORLD of Tekumel that must be sold, the images
> of an alien but enduring civilization, more detailed and realistic
> than Tolkein was in toto.


	You obviously haven't read all the supplements put out by his 
son, have you?   ;)


> Tekumel's selling strength is its richness
> of detail, the thoroughness of Barker's work.  Whereas as Tolkein
> was a linguist, Barker is a more rounded social scientist.  Middle
> Earth is a sterile place, there is no religion, but Tekumel fairly
> stinks of its people.

	Middle Earth is presented in a completely different style; after 
all, it was never intended by its author to become a role-playing game.  
Tekumel may not have started out that way too, but eventually became such.  
Hence the need for the details and "lived-in" feeling that makes Tekumel 
such a fun place to hang out for a few hours a week.  You're essentially 
comparing apples and oranges.


> Social interaction is the foundation of role
> playing: people in a room discussing what other people would or are
> doing in another situation.  Barker brings a much more convincing
> description of what people do under various conditions than nearly
> any other role playing world I have seen.  Tekumel might not be
> possible physically, but it seems plausible socially.  In a game
> that centers around character interaction, this is an important
> plus (it's kind of hard to relate, in any deep way, with a Palladin
> on a Quest for a +5 Holy Avenger).
> 

	I agree whole-heartedly with your assessment here, but obviously 
your main complaint is with D&D (or its derivatives).  Tolkien's books 
may have acted as inspiration for the first of the RPG's, but it was only 
that and no more.  It wasn't until much later that somebody thought up 
the idea of actually role-playing in Middle Earth.  The Rolemaster system 
is as cumbersome as the earlier incarnations of Tekumel's rules have 
been, and probably also contributed to their lack of wide appeal.


> Barker's is the most complete
> and well developed world on the market.


	I agree.  The only one that probably comes close are the ones put 
out by TSR and of course, MERPS.


> I am afraid that by coming out with the solo adventures
> first, TOME may have actually sabotaged the market for the rules set.
> Sell someone a game they can't play, and they won't come back.
> After nearly half a dozen such catastrophes, only us hardcore
> fanatics remain.
>

	I'm fearful of that, too.  The solo adventures work okay for 
someone with time to burn, but most of us don't have the spare time to go 
through every story-thread in every adventure in the solo books (at 
least, I haven't had the time).  And it's obviously NOT a complete 
system, so it would've discouraged me from continuing to support it, if I 
didn't already love Tekumel.

> If I were in charge of marketing Tekumel, here is what I'd do. 
 
> Paper is still superior to CD ROM, both in terms of utility and
> market penetration, so I'd publish an Encyclopedia Tekumel
> (something they would never do themselves).  I could get sales
> at $29.95, especially if it was richly illustrated and complete
> in the essential details.  I would format it much more like an
> encyclopedia, with maps, diagrams, tables, even the summary of
> linguistics.
> In order to recover more money earlier, I would sell limited edition
> numbered leathbound drafts at a higher price to people like myself.
> They would have more mistakes than the final, but fanatics would love
> to have the material.  The fanatics (and I count myself among them)
> would use the material to prepare the larger market by incorporating
> it into games and showing it off to their friends.

	Sounds good.  Once TOME has given up on Tekumel (look at the 
track record so far, and tell me I'm being pessimistic), maybe you can 
act on this idea.  It sounds like it would actually work, given enough 
starting captial.

> I haven't seen the new map yet, but I can tell you
> I still remember pulling the first map out of original EPT boxed
> set: that thing was gorgeous!


	Rather garish was my first impression, but after awhile, it did 
seem to have a beauty all of its own.....

 
> I understand that TOME can't really do this directly now: they need
> as much of that $45 as they can get to recover their costs.  But the
> market is very small, and not as many of them are going to sell as
> TOME would like.


	See my earlier comments on how long TOME will put up with their 
marketing people's rather poor handling of Tekumel.....

 
> Pictures, images, words, a vision: that's what sells about Tekumel,
> not rules.


	Right!  The vision of Tekumel must be sold; otherwise, nobody 
will see a need to buy "yet another fantasy RPG."
	I understand Professor Barker wants to have a system unique to 
his vision of Tekumel, but considering the amount of work some people 
have done to adapt it to other PROVEN systems currently on the market, 
I'm surprised he didn't try to work out some sort of deal with one of 
them.  The larger companies probably would've handled the marketing much 
better, and sales would've been much better.
	Availability of Tekumel products over the years has been 
problematic at best, and I'm very grateful to the folks at TOME for 
putting so much effort into it.  I understand their financial situation 
limits their promotional activities, but I still feel distress at knowing 
that this present successful reemergence of Tekumel will be short-lived.
	At the same time, I hope I'm completely wrong about that last 
point.  I wish, for the people at TOME, for Professor Barker, and for 
those of us who've carried the torch all these years, that this is the 
Renaissance of things Tekumel.


				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas

From barke002@maroon.tc.umn.edu Sun Apr 16 20:36:25 CDT 1995

From: barke002@maroon.tc.umn.edu
Subject: Tekumel Rules
Message-ID: <barke002-1604951244400001@dialup-5-106.gw.umn.edu>
Sender: news@news.cis.umn.edu (Usenet News Administration)
Nntp-Posting-Host: dialup-5-106.gw.umn.edu
Organization: University of Minnesota, Twin Cities
X-Newsreader: Value-Added NewsWatcher 2.0b24.0+
Date: Sun, 16 Apr 1995 17:44:40 GMT
Lines: 106

I'll repeat here part of what I rold one critic who wrote to me directly:

Neither I nor my colleague, Neil Cauley, ever expected such a flap over
"no character generator" in the new rules. I am sure TOME felt the same.
The reason was that there already IS a chaacter generation book out --
vol. 1 of the "Adventures on Tekumel" series -- and this has been out for
almost two years before the new rules set was released. It seemed clear to
us that EVERYBODY would recognise that this book would be clearly
recognised as THE character generation book. There would be no need for
another character generation book to accompany the rules -- nor even for a
quick rehash of the prior book. To please total newcomers, however, we
thought that character "archetypes" (a la Shadowrun) would be a good idea.
These contain stats, background, and pictures so that new players can get
a feel for the world without all the work of rolling up characters that
have no cultural context or personal background.

To be clear, Neil and I felt that the game should be seen as a unit in its
ENTIRETY and not just as a single stand-alone item by itself. This new
boxed set contains over 180 pages of RULES: the magic system, movement,
combat, stuff for referees, etc. These are the RULES. The character
generation system is the first book of "Adventures on Tekumel" (which also
contains background material). The creatures and alien races are covered
by the Bestiary. The second, third, and fourth volumes of the "Adventures
on Tekumel" series contain more cultural background: how the temples work,
the clans, the Tsolyani army, how to shop, what various foreign lands look
like, etc. I thought it would be clear that these items are all PART of a
single GREATER gaming unit: a mega-game, if you will. All in one box, they
would have been too hideously expensive for anybody but the richest and
most committed. As separate units, they can be purchased over a period of
time -- or not at all. The character generation book is not necessary to
those willing to explore the archetypes. The Bestiary can be ignored if
one already has the old EPT rules (although the materials in there are, in
my opinion, very sketchy).The other volumes of the Solitaire Adventures
set can be used to build characters with experience, possessions, and
talents -- or they can be ignored, and purely "gamed" experienece can be
substituted. Whatever people want...

I am really surprised that the structure just described has not been clear
>from  the beginning: a central set of rules, surrounded by a number of
booklets and game-aids. This has been an industry standard for many, many
years: a central "game-book," with handooks on the gods, various special
"castles" or locales, etc. These satellites are not in themselves
expensive by today's standards. It costs over $500 to equip oneself with
all that is needed to play some of the other major games on the market --
they just don't say so. All of the Tekumel satellites can be had for about
$100, and the new rules for $45 -- with some discounts from TOME if
purchased together. Compared with other games, I don't see this as a
"rip-off." The wole set of Tekumel materials can be had for comparatively
little, considering inflation. And while few would stand still for a boxed
set including ALL of these booklets (at a price of $175???), many will be
able to buy first one piece and then another, and will eventually own the
whole set.

I wish we could have included the creature dscriptions, the world
descriptions, the history, etc. etc. in this latest work, but this would
have increased the cost of the boxed set by three or four times! The
creatures were only sketched in the most rudimentary way in "Empire of the
Petal Throne." The same was true of the history of Tekumel. I have been
trying to persudade TOME to reissue the 3 volumes of the old Sourcebook --
they have 2 in stock, but they never published the third. I suspect now,
with all the poor reviews of this game, that they never will.

If buyers are not satisfied, they should call TOME at 610-935-7622 and get
their money back. If the character generation book is not on sale in a
particular game store, I can only urge that new players use the character
archetypes until they can order one from TOME, or just build a campaign
around the rather interesting people of the Archtypes themselves. If this
works for "Shadowrun," why not for Tekumel?

I don't consider the new game "incomplete." It is part of a large
constellation of rules and game-aids. I thought this would be crystal
clear from the way the previous solitaire adventures, bestiary, and
character generation book appeared. 

TOME is a small company, without the artists, editors, co-writers, or
capital to produce major games. They operate on the proverbial shoestring.
I personally enjoyed the covers and the archetypes artwork. The map is, in
my opinion, very handsome. I have seen a lot worse among the big games
currently stocked in our local gaming store. 

I have no idea why the dice. That wasn't my idea.

All of the "satellite" books are available from TOME: Ebon Bindings, the
Character Generation booklet, the Bestiary, the other 3 volumes of the
solo adventures (which are really pretty much "background materials" in
disguise). I think many will be willing to try out the Archetypes. Others
will ask their store to obtain the character generation book -- and a few,
yes, a few will return the game for their money back. So be it.

It was all I could do to get Tekumel out again in SOME form before the
public before I die (I am now retired and ill with a variety of problems).
I am saddened by all of these negative comments, but I still think we did
the right thing. If I had had lots of money and lots of support
(co-writers, several artists, etc.), as do some other major games, I might
have done differently. But this is all I can manage. I can only hope that
players will be patient and interested enough to obtain the new rules and
also some of the other pieces to the set. I think Tekumel will reward
them. It's an interesting and different world.

This will be my last word on this topic. I have said my piece. Please
don't bother e-mailing me about this. If you don't enjoy the new rules
(plus or minus the other satellites), please return them to TOME. I hope
more of you will use them for what they were meant for and enjoy.

-- 
M. A. R. Barker

From teller@silvercaw.pn.com Tue Apr 18 18:15:27 CDT 1995

From: teller@silvercaw.pn.com (Joseph Teller)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Re: What Tekumel needs is a magazine
Distribution: WORLD
Message-ID: <797875604.479snx@silvercaw.pn.com>
References: <barke002-1304951808470001@dialup-2-103.gw.umn.ed
Date: Fri, 14 Apr 95 16:06:44 GMT

Lines: 38

In article <barke002-1304951808470001@dialup-2-103.gw.umn.ed barke002@maroon.tc.umn.edu writes:
>
>Again, as has been said elsewhere, what Tekumel needs most is MONEY. A
>magazine cannot be produced without MONEY. This, we ain''t got. With the
>sort of investment one of the big companies can throw into a game ANYTHING
>can be done. I have approved ideas for magazines, modules, computer games,
>and all sorts of other game-aids, but these take perseverance and talent
>to produce, then they take MONEY. TOME, at least, is trying to produce the
>basics.
>
>-- 
>M. A. R. Barker

Agreed in full that money is the problem, and part of the reason why it
is a problem is because far too many people in the gaming world demand
extremely high production values.

We've been arguing this one on my own gaming mail list for some time, in
regards to my own game world & system. People either wanted extemely
high production values or they wanted everything for free. No one was
willing to accept various offered middle of the road approaches (Like
desktop published copies or electronic copies) if there was money
involved. The gaming public has become jaded by the 'frills' of
production, wanting full color art, fancy bindings (or hard back books),
etc.

I though the production values on the Different Worlds versions of
Tekumel were fine, doable within the capabilities of modern desktop
publishing (though maybe with spiral bindings instead of the staples)
and viable. It seems in this market I'm in a minority.

Quality of writing, material and content seems to be secondary to many
gamers these days. They'll put up with abysmal and flawed mechanics and
world concepts (Like the 'World of Darkness') for flashy production.

The market is no longer one of hobbyists, and that makes those of us
who are in an uncomfortable minority.

>   No background of Tekumel

    A ridiculous ommission.

 the game is not playable by new folks.

>
>First an overall comment on the 3 books. Compared to most other RPG's the

>glossy cover. About the same as Deluxe RQ books that AH brought out 10

>RPG's of the late 70's some of it good, most fairly poor. 

Sounds much like much of the Different Worlds editions, in regards to
binding etc.

[[Excess omitted that I wasn't commenting on]]

Basically you have 3 booklets with a grand total of about 200 pages
of material, including artwork and with no indexing.

>The map as mentioned above is two-sided, full-color, glossy 17"x21" in
>size. It is very nice. No hexes, so keep the old map around for distances,
>but I love this map. Some real nice cartography really adds to the feel of
>the world. You can really appreciate the difficulty the Tsolyani faced in
>invading Yan Kor. The front contains Livyanu, Shenyu, Mu'ugalavya, Yan
>Kor, Tsolyanu, and the western part of Salarvya. The reverse contains the
>remainder of Salarvya, THe plains of Glass, Mihallu, and the rest. No new
>territory, just the same as the old map but completely different. The map
>is also surrounded by glyphs of the 10 gods and 10 cohorts on front and
>other stylized symbols on the back. I'm not sure exactly what they are but
>they are pretty.

The map sounds nice, but it seems by the description they put a lot of
the production money into it, which may be part of the problem. Some of
us wouldn't care if it was simply a black and white map, so long as it
was readable.

>The box is full color, both top and bottom. The front shows some
>adventures encountering the Hokun via tube-car and they aren't in good
>shape. Unfortunately, I don't like this particular piece of artwork. The
>back is much nicer (TOME used it in their flyer) and is a picture of a
>young girl being dressed with a city with its pyarmids in the background.
>Very nice.

 And again, too much in the way of 'production draw'...usually done to
 make up for a lack of content when you are dealing with a 'box'. I know
 lots of folks that avoid sealed boxes when buying RPG material because
 it is usually to hide a lack of content.

>Over all I rate this RPG as very disappointing. I don't feel ripped-off
>and deceived like a previous poster, but after waiting so long I am quite
>sad, since this game won't sell. People expect more from their game
>systems these days. It would have been a great achievement for 1975, but
>for 1995, it is third-rate. I can forgive the somewhat cheap components.
>Tekumel has limited appeal and TOME is hedging their investment. Gamers
>expect more than is given in this set. Non-Tekumel fans won't touch this
>game, and why should they, when vastly superior products are on the market
>at a lower cost. I was very excited when I got home this evening and found
>that the game had arrived. Now I am very sad, since I see this as the end
>of the line for Tekumel products. This game won't sell at all well, thus
>TOME will give up on Tekumel, sigh! What I thought was a new beginning,
>now seems like the end.

 Agreed on your analysis, I'm sorry to say.

 At $44 a copy the system is overpriced in regards to content. White
 Wolf produced Vampire in Hardback (no map or silly dice) for a retail
 cover of $25, containing 275 pages, for example. I see no reason why
 Tekumel could not have been done in a similar style and cost factor.

 If cheaper production values were used (which it appears was done
 with Tekumel this time in regards to the books) and the silly frills
 (Dice, complex map) were disposed of, the product should be possible
 at much lower costs. I know this from my own exploration into this
 for my own game (Fantasy Realms : World of T'Phon). Tome must have
 paid far too much for its artists, or wanted too large a profit margin,
 or had distributors and retailers that wanted too big a profit margin.



From erich@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu Tue Apr 18 18:15:30 CDT 1995
Article: 322 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!news.tamu.edu!erich
From: erich@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu (Erich Schneider)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Columbia's "Harn" as a model for Tekumel publishing
Date: 17 Apr 1995 04:11:36 GMT
Organization: Texas A&M University, Hypermedia Research Lab
Lines: 67
Distribution: world
Message-ID: <ERICH.95Apr16231136@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu>
NNTP-Posting-Host: hrl9.cs.tamu.edu

What do those of you who know both think of Columbia's "Encyclopedia
Harnica" as a model of FRP world-publishing that Tekumel publishers
might want to emulate?

For those who don't know: Columbia Games publishes a game,
"Harnmaster"; aside from a few items which are primarily rules (core
rules, rules for naval/seafaring topics, and more detailed magic
rules) most of the materials are descriptions of a particular region
of the fantasy world of Kethira, an archipelago dominated by the
island of Harn (similar in technical and social development to 
England under the Normans). 

The bulk of the descriptive materials are the "kingdom modules" (one
of which is actually a "republic module"), each containing several
articles pertaining to topics related to the kingdom in question.  The
modules are designed to be cut apart, hole-punched, and alphabetized
into binders.  Typically, a module has a longer article on the kingdom
itself (its history, feudal structure, descriptions of its major
personalities and subregions, and some numerical data on those
regions), articles on two or three of the major communities, one on a
ruin or other mysterious site, very short articles (two-page) on the
nomadic human peoples (two or three) near the kingdom, and one or two
articles on another topic related to the region (things like the Guild
of Arcane Lore, the gladiatorial Pamesani Games, the island's systems
of law, common medicinal herbs, Harnic heraldry, Harnic astrology,
details on the elves and dwarves (described in their kingdom modules),
etc.).

Other materials include "Gods of Harn", with articles describing
"religion on Harn" and the major deities, "Cities of Harn" and "Son of
Cities", describing the seven major towns of the island and some major
buildings in them, "Castles of Harn" and "Castles of Orbaal" (Orbaal
is one of the kingdoms), and the overall "Harnworld" module which
describes the island's overall history, the continent it's near
(Lythia), its world (Kethira), and a very general article on the
world's languages. Products on the scale of "Harnworld" have also been
done on the Viking-ish region of Ivinia and the more traditionally
feudal Shorkyne/Chelemby/Harbaal region. There's also a "HarnPlayer"
product, containing general background material oriented toward
players and a bunch of commonly-known stories and legends of the
island.

I think this could be a viable model for developing Tekumel - in fact,
things have sort of been going along these lines with the S&G1
sourcebook, the bestiary, and the religion book (still in the
future). Tsolyanu is already divided along provincial lines, and S&G1
has one-liner descriptions of "interesting stuff" in each region of
the country. Perhaps the provinces could be grouped into larger chunks
and Encyclopedia Harnica-style modules written for them, with another
describing the nation's history in general. This way, gamers could get
information on the regions their campaigns are set in, and gradually
acquire more pieces depending on how interested they are in the "big
picture". If this works, one could go on to develop the other four
Empires and the minor states to various degrees.

I think it's important that things be clustered by the publisher on a
basis of game usefulness rather than some more artificial scheme
("Scrolls of Knowledge A-C", "Scrolls of Knowledge D-F", etc.). 

TOME can take comfort in the fact that they can't possibly fail to
adhere to schedules as badly as Columbia - Harn fans are still waiting
for the Trierzon and Azeryan regional modules, first slated to come
out in 1986!
--
Erich Schneider  erich@bush.cs.tamu.edu  http://bush.cs.tamu.edu/~erich

"The Hierophant is Disguised and Confused."

I am still awaiting the new rules, but I read the long review posted
with interest. I am quite pleased the Adventures In Tekumel Vol 1 is
not wasted, I always feared an alternative character gen system for
the new rules.

Templates a la Star Wars / Shadowrun sound very good, and indeed any shop 
willing to stock the new rules will be able to get the character gen.

I really am surprised that people expected huge budget production 
values. Tekumel just isn;t like that, half of it's charm is the fact
that there are acres of dusty tomes in close type that you have to study
hard.

I am very much looking forward to a game system that I can play, with good
magic rules. The S&G magic was never available and yet that is what other
fans have raved about.

I agree that Chaosium would have done a slicker job, but even they would
have had to charge a lot, cut out a lot of the interesting stuff, and
maybe had to think very hard about whether to bother.

Thank you TOME, Thank you Prof Barker, I love your world with all its
imperfections, and I hope that the criticism will not hurt you too much.
People on the 'net can be very critical, more so than if they were face to
face.

Can I hpe that you might honour us with having more Tekumel material
donated to your fans? I guess much of it is typewritten stuff, perhaps
Bob Dushay could ask your permission to scan it, even convert it to
wordprocessor files?

In article <3mjlf7$gsj@donald.cc.utexas.edu>, resmith@donald.cc.utexas.edu (Robert Smith) writes:
>I was flipping through a travel magazine the other day and came upon an article
>on fungi. This got me to thinking about the use of fungi as food on Tekumel.
>I began to wonder if this might have some religious connotations. Some of the
>ideas I have begun to develop are as follows:
> 
[Intriguing speculations of fungi deleted]
> 
>Appearances of Fungi
>Tekumelyani fungi are at least as diverse as those found on earth. An edible
>mushroom particularly favored by Sarku worshippers and found only in the
>underworld is known as the Deathhead, because it vaguely resembles as
>small human skull. Another, the Scepter of Belkhanu, appears as a long staff
>topped by a small golden knob. Some edible fungi have disguised themselves as
>food of the Ssu, so the collector must be very careful in his attempts to
>harvest.

I'll say "the collector must be very careful", Prof. Barker himself
mentions fungi as a hazard of the underworld in at least one place that
I recall (_The Man of Gold_), and one of the nastier denizens of the
underworld is a form of animate fungi (the Sagun): caveat Mycophage! ;-)

Interesting speculation though, as fungi have played such important 
roles in the diets and religions of Earth, why not Tekumel?  Though, the 
comparative prevalence of edible vs. nasty fungi might mitigate against 
them being widely used.

>Just some initial thoughts on an admittedly odd topic.
>Any additional thoughts or comments are welcome and encouraged. Maybe I'll
>experiment with some recipes and post those as well.
> 
>Rob

Best,

-* Stephen *-
Stephen Posey
SLP@uno.edu
University of New Orleans


From gauntlet@bga.com Tue Apr 18 18:15:36 CDT 1995

Subject: Shut up and play! ;-)
Date: 17 Apr 1995 18:08:00 GMT

Hey everybody.  Just play the game.  If you don't like some of the rules, 
fiddle with 'em.  It's a grand tradition in the gaming hobby to tinker 
with game mechanics.  If you don't want to pay that much for a set of 
rules you're probably going to change, don't buy it - get the source 
material and use a different system.  But for gods' sake, if you're into 
Tekumel, SUPPORT IT!  I can't believe all the bitching I'm reading in 
here.  We should all be thanking our lucky stars that there's anything 
new coming out at all!  If you want that to keep happening, *complaining* 
won't do it, and suggesting other ways the game *could have* been 
packaged won't do it.  The only thing that'll keep Tekumel stuff coming 
out is if there continues to be enough interest in it.  So play the 
game, introduce as many friends as possible to Tekumel, and help nurture a 
feeling of excitement about Prof. Barker's world.  If you can't do that, 
Tekumel's *already* dead.  Right?

You know what I'd like to see?  Some war stories from ongoing campaigns.  
Neato ideas for artifacts and wierd new monsters and stuff.  Things that 
remind us all that we're actually interested in playing games set in 
Tekumel instead of bitching about production values and so on. And I'll 
tell you something else - when they finally deliver my boxed set, I 
intend to love it to death, whether it's incomplete or unattractive or 
overpriced or whatever.  It's TEKUMEL, dammit!

WWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWW

        gauntlet@bga.com        Sic Gorgiamus Subjectatus Allos Nunc

	For the past two days I have been following the bitching about 
the new edition of the rules.  I have one thing to ask all of you:
When you go to McDonalds and order an extra value meal do you bitch
that you didn't get prime rib?  This is what you are doing over the new
rules!  Face reality.  These rules are for NEW players.  How many copies
would have been sold if these were for "Expericed Tekumel Players Only"?
The only way that Tekumel will survive as a game is if NEW players are
brought into the fold.  Haveing Arctype templates and not chariter creation
rules is to make it easyer for newbies to get into the system.  Having a
box over a bag makes people want to look at it.  Having dice in the box
means "everthing needed to play included".  Yes it would be nice to have
more background books.  But the only way TOME will be able to afford to
produce these is if there is high enough demand for it.  Adding new players
into the fold increases the demand for the advance stuff.

	As for the argument over Tekumel needing a magazine.  There are
indepentet magazines.  Write Tekamel articals for them.  Subment your
favoret adventures to them.  Subment your Tekumel art to them. (That's
for you Jeff Dee.  I know you can draw).  Bring Tekumel to people who
may never hear of it anyother way.  A good adventure in a magazine is 
better advertising than any slick ad.  We all think that the world of Tekumal
is uneaqualed ion role playing,  Let the most fasinating world sell itself
by bring it to players who are unaware of it.  This is what needs to be done
for Tekumel products to be produced.

	Just my 2 cents worth.  I turn the soapbox over to the next clown

From anton@infoserv.com Wed Apr 19 14:23:21 CDT 1995
Article: 329 of alt.games.frp.tekumel

X-Mailer: TMail version 1.13
From: "Anton Dovydaitis" <anton@infoserv.com>
Organization: American Youth GO Association
References: <wdf-1504950002010001@192.0.2.1> <797984457.483snx@silvercaw.pn.com>
Subject: Re: REVIEW - Gardasiyal The new RPG rules (long)

In <797984457.483snx@silvercaw.pn.com>, teller@silvercaw.pn.com (Joseph Teller)  wrote:
> 
>  At $44 a copy the system is overpriced in regards to content. White
>  Wolf produced Vampire in Hardback (no map or silly dice) for a retail
>  cover of $25, containing 275 pages, for example. I see no reason why
>  Tekumel could not have been done in a similar style and cost factor.

Economies of scale.  White Wolf has MUCH larger economies of scale than
TOME, probably by an order of magnitude or more.

For example, my company publishes books on GO, which is still fairly
obscure in the West (although it is the HOTTEST sport in Asia).
Print runs are in the low to mid thousands, and the end price to our
retail customers for a paperback book is $14.95.  Yet chess publishers
can sell much thicker books for half that price.  Another example.
I have to print 5,000 copies of a color flyer for our GO software.
The first 5,000 copies are $475, the next 5,000 are only $200 more.
The next 10,000 copies would ALSO be only $200 more.

>  If cheaper production values were used (which it appears was done
>  with Tekumel this time in regards to the books) and the silly frills
>  (Dice, complex map)

I haven't seen the new map, but I remember the absolute THRILL of pulling
the original vinyl map out of the very first EPT box back in the 70's.
I STILL remember how it smelled.

Given the materials that TOME already has, it should consider shrinkwrapping
the map and the first volume of the Solo Adventures together, and see if
they can't use THAT to market the game better.

>  or had distributors and retailers that wanted too big a profit margin.

Distributors and retails REQUIRE a reasonable profit margin.  Wargames
West would like to buy my GO books at 55-60% off retail, and won't buy
at 50%.  Game stores buy my books at 40-45% off, but would prefer 50%.
Why would a store accept lower margins for one product when it can
instead spend its dollars on products with 50% margins?

If TOME has similar requirements to Ishi Press, then they're selling
it for 40% of retail to distribution, or $17.60.  TOME's margin can't
be any worse than 40% (otherwise it's not worth doing business) so
it cannot cost them more than $11 to produce, including overhead and
royalties.  And that's assuming that it moves in anything like reasonable
or expected quantities.  Which, at this point, I doubt.

From erich@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu Sat Apr 22 15:25:28 CDT 1995
Article: 333 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!news.tamu.edu!erich
From: erich@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu (Erich Schneider)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: "facing reality" was Re: Shut up and play! ;-)
Date: 19 Apr 1995 00:45:39 GMT
Organization: Texas A&M University, Hypermedia Research Lab
Lines: 64
Message-ID: <ERICH.95Apr18194539@hrl9.cs.tamu.edu>
References: <3muaq0$q7f@giga.bga.com> <3n1fsc$dtt@pentagon.io.com>
NNTP-Posting-Host: hrl9.cs.tamu.edu
In-reply-to: davis@pentagon.io.com's message of 18 Apr 1995 17:53:00 -0500

In article <3n1fsc$dtt@pentagon.io.com> davis@pentagon.io.com (No One) writes:

>Face reality.  These rules are for NEW players.  How many copies would
>have been sold if these were for "Expericed Tekumel Players Only"?
>The only way that Tekumel will survive as a game is if NEW players are
>brought into the fold.  Haveing Arctype templates and not chariter
>creation rules is to make it easyer for newbies to get into the
>system.  Having a box over a bag makes people want to look at it.
>Having dice in the box means "everthing needed to play included".  Yes
>it would be nice to have more background books.

You state the game is "for NEW players", and that the inclusion of
dice makes "everything needed to play included". However, I would say
a character generation system is considered "needed to play" by most
serious RPG players (i.e. people who have played other games and now
want to try Tekumel), and it's damned tough to play a game set on
Tekumel when the spiffy "everything needed to play" game one just
bought has nothing in it on the world one is supposed to be playing
in.

You ask how many copies would be sold if the rules were for the
experienced Tekumel player only - yet Professor Barker has effectively
stated that he expects everyone who picks these up to either have all
the solo adventures, or to acquire them in short order.

Yes, _Star Wars: the RPG_, _TORG_, and _Shadowrun_, among others, use
the "template"/"archetype" concept. However, they also have rules for
creating totally new characters from ground zero. Said games have a
growth path from novice to experienced player that can be experienced
with the basic rules alone (I say this with some reservation, as both
_TORG_ and _Shadowrun_ didn't include fully fleshed-out magic systems,
including spell design rules, in their basic rules). If one is aiming
for broad appeal, this seems to me a better strategy than one which
produces a product containing materials useful primarily for novices
(and even then questionably so, from what I've heard) and which says
to the more experienced player, "to play this game at your level, you
have to buy more stuff".

I will probably buy _Gardasiyal_ to support TOME, Prof. Barker, and
Tekumel, and to satisfy my own completionist tendencies. However, from
what I hear, I very much doubt it will be the "breakout product" that
Tekumel boosters seem to have been hoping for. I also think TOME is
being deceptive if they don't emphasize on the box cover (which I
assume will be shrink-wrapped to disallow possible purchaser
inspection of its contents) that it contains rules only, minus a
character generation system, and has no world background.

Also, when gamers buy a rules set priced well above the average price
of an RPG basic rules set these days, they are justified in expecting
not necessarily "prime rib" but definitely something more than an
"extra value meal"; I don't believe _Gardasiyal_ is being pushed as
such, either.

(As an aside, I hope I'm not the only one who thought the bad puns in
the solo adventures got really old, really fast, and who hopes they
have been toned way way down in _Gardasiyal_.)
--
Erich Schneider  erich@bush.cs.tamu.edu  http://bush.cs.tamu.edu/~erich

"You are a true believer. Blessings of the State; blessings of the
masses.  Thou art a subject of the Divine, created in the image of
Man, by the masses, for the masses. Let us be thankful we have
commerce. Buy more. Buy more now. Buy. And be happy."
            - Confession booth blessing, _THX-1138_

	Bill,
	Thanks for your review of Gardasiyal.  I've only just started 
reading over the rules, but I was also disappointed with the same items 
you've mentioned.  The fact that you have to get the Adventures Book #1 
even to generate characters is infuriating!  I already have the book, but 
folks new to Tekumel obviously won't.  My set came with an order form so 
you could buy that book directly from TOME, but how many new folks will 
feel that this should've been included in their $45 purchase already?
	The rules do seem to be a very trimmed-down version of S&G, and 
perhaps that's a good thing.  I remember those rules being extremely 
over-cumbersome and many of the rules unnecessary.  Having a quick-play 
set of combat rules is actually good for folks who don't care about which 
knuckle on your right pinky finger got bruised in that last combat round.
	As I mentioned in an earlier post, I felt that the past track 
record of Tekumel with small game companies was a good indication how 
this go at writing a "definitive" set of rules would turn out.  If TSR 
(probably the biggest of the gaming companies) did such a mediocre job 
with 2nd Ed. AD&D, we shouldn't be surprised when a much smaller company 
doesn't meet our expectations.
	I am very thankful to TOME for making every effort to reawaken 
interest in the world of Tekumel.  I just wish the effort had produced a 
product that would be cutting-edge for 1995.  Instead, we have a rules 
set that is somewhat patchwork and incomplete, which will not appeal to 
the vital new blood needed to make it profitable.
	As Bill said, *Very Heavy Sigh!*

				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas

	I will be at Gen-Con, and will be looking forward to seeing any 
sort of presentation of the world of Tekumel.  I remember the early years 
of Gen-Con, when there would be a full-scale battle set up, and you could 
come along and help push pieces around for as long as you wished.
	Normally, the battle revolved around taking a small fortress on a 
Sakbe road, with only a few hundred units on each side.  It was still 
loads of fun to watch or participate; the road and fortress were finely 
detailed, and the minis were exquisitely painted!
	At a local gaming convention here in St. Louis a bunch of years 
ago, we had the Tekumel Games folks attending.  They brought a complete 
model of a temple dedicated to Vimuhla!  It could be taken apart to show 
various portions of the interior, including some of the dungeons.
	If any of you are attending Gen-Con, let me know so I can look 
you up.  I'm trying to generate new interest here in playing in the world 
of Tekumel, but swapping ideas and stories is always helpful.

				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas

In article <3n0m80$1sk@gap.cco.caltech.edu>, ral@alumni.caltech.edu says...
>
>When EPT first came out (from TSR, for The Strategic Review)
>there were some great maps on oil cloth or plastic backed
>cloth.  Has there been a consideration of doing a reprint 
>of those?  the art work of the new maps is great, but they
>may not have the durability of those old maps.  This may
>have actually been done in the couple of decades I have been 
>away.  In any case, is anyone selling the old maps or newer
>reprints of them?  Or was there another set of maps done on
>durable backing that are the current vogue?

The maps are a bit of an issue.  I've not seen the new ones yet, but 
personally I think we should be grateful that there now are some.

I know the original EPT came with two maps in colour - one of Jakalla, and 
one of Tsolyanu.  The Gamescience reprint came with these as well. I have 
one, so I can testify that the maps were the only good quality bit of the 
Gamescience reprint.  I expect they may have been the same ones as the 
original - in any event they were printed in full colour on tough plastic.

Gamescience also issued the Tekumel World Book (aka Swords and Glory Vol I) 
in a boxed set with 4 maps of Tekumel, covering a lot more ground.  These 
maps too were of excellent quality, unlike the hideous typesetting and 
binding (only those who have one know how awful these were - buy the DW 
reprints where possible).

The Different Worlds reprint of EPT did not come with any maps - only a 
photocopy onto brown card (?) of the Jakalla map, bound as an insert.  Nor 
did their reprint of 2 parts (of 3) of the world book.  I think these 3 
books are still available.

So I can say you've chosen an excellent moment to return to EPT.  For the 
first time in years there is a load of good quality material available; even 
some colour maps!

Check out the archives of the tekumel newsletter for details on what has 
been published, and by whom, since you last played.

Something like that, posted carefully only to pertinent newsgroups, gets
two thumbs up from me.  It's these pinheads who blanket the newsfeed with
their nonsequitur all-caps rantings.

From alberti@riverside.mr.net Sat Apr 22 15:25:33 CDT 1995
Article: 341 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!news.media.mit.edu!grapevine.lcs.mit.edu!uhog.mit.edu!news.mtholyoke.edu!news.umass.edu!caen!usenet.cis.ufl.edu!usenet.eel.ufl.edu!spool.mu.edu!howland.reston.ans.net!math.ohio-state.edu!scipio.cyberstore.ca!skypoint.com!news3.mr.net!mr.net!riverside.mr.net!alberti
From: alberti@riverside.mr.net (Bob Alberti)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Wading into battle
Date: 19 Apr 1995 15:16:31 GMT
Organization: Minnesota Regional Network
Lines: 99
Message-ID: <3n39gf$ci9@cedar.mr.net>
NNTP-Posting-Host: riverside.mr.net
X-Newsreader: TIN [version 1.2 PL2]

Okay, here's my take, briefly, on the whole TOME-boxed-set issue:

"You can't please everyone, so you've got to please yourself."
"Something is better than nothing."
"Caveat emptor."
"I never buy version .0 of anything."

First, everyone who is interested enough to buy the boxed set IN ADVANCE
has had two or more years to examine the solo adventure books, even if only
by looking at them in the bookstore.  These clearly state that they are
the preliminary rule-set for the more advanced rules, including character
generation and rules for low-level characters.

Barring this, TOME's telephone number is readily available, as is their
address.  Prior to purchasing the product, one could have asked here on
the newsgroup or directly of TOME what the boxed set contained.  If one
insists on being the first-on-the-block to see the new rules, one must
be willing to accept what one gets.  If you were unwilling to accept
what you got, why didn't you wait for someone else to review the product
for you, and decide based on more information?

IN ANY EVENT...  this set of publications is the first new release of
Tekumel in many years.  Whether or not it is perfect, whether or not
it's done the way this self-appointed expert or that one believes is
proper, it is a GOOD THING.  Why?

Because it makes Tekumel a modern product.  Rather than being "that old
game from the Seventies" it is now something which is currently in-print
and on the market.

Why is this good?  Because as many people have pointed out, it would be
lovely if someone with more money than TOME were to invest more in 
Tekumel and "do it right".  Or at least "do it bigger."  With Tekumel 
currently in-print, it's much more likely that a bigger game company 
might look at it as an existing product which they could purchase the
rights to and publish.  Is that likely to actually happen?  Maybe not.
But it's a lot more likely than it was before TOME took up the challenge
of producing something as big as Tekumel.

Personally, I'd love to see some huge company come along and offer both
TOME and Barker sufficient compensation to transfer the rights to Tekumel.
Done right, Tekumel could be a uniquely successful product for a company
with foresight and good marketing.

Finally, bickering over the rules is silly.  Tekumel is not about rules.
This will make many self-appointed experts purse their lips and shake
their heads, but it's the truth.  Tekumel is about the culture.  If you
buy Tekumel game books to find out exactly how many "hits" a chlen-hide
shield has, or exactly how far a '16' roll allows you to jump, you're
playing the wrong game.  Tekumel products should best be used as a 
reference to the culture, a window into this weird, amazing world.  What
does a Mnor LOOK like, not how many hit points does it have.  What
takes place during the Festival of Light in Usenanu, not how many Qirgal
it costs for a paper boat with a candle in it.  As has been stated over
and over again, Phil's group doesn't even USE the rules -- any rules.
Sometimes we'll look up a detail or that, but without rulebooks we'd
manage to figure it out for ourselves.  But where we need BOOKS is when
we're trying to figure out the significance of a particular ritual celebration
to the residents of a city, how we ought to properly approach a powerful 
individual for their support doing something which might be treasonous but
which is motivated by allegance to the Petal Throne, if not the Emperor.
It's in the workings of the culture that the real questions exist.

And, frankly, as a cultural reference, the solo books are unequaled.
They are the Professor's own examples of how the people of Tekumel interact
under conditions both extreme (as in the novels) and mundane.  THAT is what
one needs for Tekumel.

So the rules-lawyers and RPG experts can complain all they like about this-
or-that characteristic of the game and how it is constructed or marketed.
There is no pleasing all such people, and any change made in one direction
would irritate adherents of other gaming techniques and philosophies.
And, sure, we'd all like to see so much money invested in Tekumel publications
that each page was glossy paper and featured photographs of beautiful people
in various states of undress with rules written by Paid Experts, delivered
to your home on a palanquin borne by nude slaves and opened to a fanfare of
a-cappella singers and a release of doves.

Meanwhile, the rest of us should focus on what we do have.  First, NEW STUFF.
Second, MORE INFORMATION THAN WE HAD BEFORE, and third the OPPORTUNITY to
see Tekumel furthered.

If you happen to know someone with connections to powerful game-publishing
companies, show them the TOME stuff.  Maybe a big company will buy Tekumel
and "do it right", even to hiring the 'experts' on here as advisors for 
huge salaries.  Maybe Spielberg will make a movie out of Tekumel under his
new studio system and I'll get to play a slave.  But until then, PLAY THE
GAME.  Enjoy!  That's what it's really about.


P.S. Personally, I think the new maps make the whole thing worth it.

P.P.S. If it makes the game more attractive to you, be aware that
several of the models for the archetype illustrations are real women
who you could meet someday if you're lucky.  Woo hoo!

Professor Barker,

I'd like to personally thank you for your gift in bestowing Tekumel upon
the gaming community. I find the history fascinating and devoured the only
two novels I ever found (_The Man of Gold_ and _Flamesong_). I am saddened
to hear of your ill health and wish you all the best. I wish we could have
met.


To the rest of you,

I have not gamed in almost ten years now, but still follow the
discussions.I have to say a few words about the industry. Not that much
has changed really since I stopped. Too many people want everything handed
to them on a silver platter and even then couldn't run an interesting
campaign, then they blame the system for what are truly their own
shortcomings.

That said, there were indeed problems in the early EPT rules I had. There
were many things I didn't like about about EVERY system I picked up (at
least 10 RPG systems). So myself and one other guy wrote our own. It too
wasn't perfect, but there was nobody else to complain to, and most folks
who played it thought it worked pretty well. Moral of the story: If you
don't like something about a system, CHANGE IT. It is after all, your
world.

I just recieved the boxed set today and while I was already expecting the
worse since reading these "reviews", I was not really all that displeased.
I think that the Archetypes serve their purpose well. 

But, I agree with Mr. Alberti, that the true need that MUST be fulfilled
is in actual source material. Now, before the large cry goes out
concerning the HUGE source published and republished, I submit that while
copious, that source book was necessarily large to encompass such a
complex, far ranging, and dynamic world. I refer more towards the
focussing on a certain section, town, or city. Detail the political
intrigues running rampant in said city, and design some interesting NPCs
to be encountered there. I could go on with more examples, but I think you
get my point.

I will support Tekumel in whatever form it appears in and frankly this new
game will give me the excuse of introducing Tekumel to new players. being
a "new" game rather than "that game from the seventies" does entice new
players. I know it doesn't make sense, but it's true.

So, my congratulations to the Professor. Long may his vision ensnare and
enthrall our imaginations.

What *really* annoys me (having just got my pre-order copy airmail - I paid
for it, so I'm entitled to bitch about it!) is the *really* poor level of
typesetting shown in Gardasiyal compared to the previous Tekumel releases by
TOME. I can (and do) better using a PC and MS Publisher or Ventura Publisher
(which seems to be what they used ... a PC and a Page Layout program) - the
ragged right layout and wide margins that waste so much space are a real
annoyance ... they could have fitted at least 10-15% *more* in (or done it
at less cost) if they had used the same layout as for the previous books
(which at least looked professional). And some of the tables have columns
of figures that don't even match up with the column headers! This is piss
poor production planning. The whole product looks like some juvie just
threw it together overnight ... surely they could have done better.

As for the fact that the boxed set is completely unusable for a person that
buys it off the shelf, well, this was completely inexcusable. It bodes ill
for the future of Tekumel products if this is the "standard" to which they
aspire. I sure as hell hope that Mitlaniyal (the God handbook) is going to
be done to the standard of the previous products.

Also, I note in an insert in Gadarsiyal that the three books inside are being
sold separately ... there's no chance, I s'pose, of the separate versions
having being printed with decent, non-self-destruct, covers? Anyone know?
As it is, I'll be having mine photocopied and ring bound as the chance of
the three books surviving extended use is, as far as I can see, zilch.

Finally, has anyone else suggested to TOME that they need to bring out some
sort of historical background/setting *update* to cover the world of
Tekumel as it is *now*. I have the original TSR rules, the DW reprints,
Gamescience's "Swords & Glory" materials ... and the little driblets of
clues dropped in the solitaire adventures are *really* intriguing, and vastly
annoying because they don't tell enough! How hard could it be to do an update?

But for ghu's sake don't do it as *another* solitaire adventure ... I find
them a complete bore and probably wouldn't buy any further ones just on
general principles!

Phil McGregor

Subject: Another naive suggestion (or 3) from Texas
Date: 21 Apr 1995 06:38:15 GMT

Greetings!

I believe that in this day and age, an out of print book is an
abomination that must not happen except for materials that are harmful
to society.  The choice of which books fall into that category are left
to the Reader WITH THE EXCEPTION of any material related to Empire of
the Petal Throne and the World of Tekumel.

How about an alt.games.frp.tekumel-sponsored reprint of some of the
extremely difficult to find (in Dallas, anyway) out-of-print background
materials?  For example, we locate the copyright owners of the "NW
Frontier Gazeteer" and "Journal of Tekumel Affairs" (and any other
publication that can be found) and offer to buy inexpensively offset
printed copies printed by a printer of Professor Barker's choice
(perhaps TOME?) and pay them a royalty per copy equal to what the
copyright holder got off the original, out-of-print version.  Plus the
cost of the copy.  

These inexpensive copies would be designed not to compete with the
market for rare items except that the gaming material would be
available to the masses.  I am suggesting that all reproductions ne
made in black and white on 8.5"x11" paper with a light cardstock cover
if appropriate.  Perhaps some materials would not be appropriate to
copy and would be left out-of-print?

I have assumed a lot, but if we arrange it correctly, the majority of
Tekumel-related material could be made available under terms that would
benefit all.  Those who own the rights to the material would profits
they would not otherwise receive.  Those who want the material would
profit from materials they could not otherwise obtain.  Interest would
rise in the game as this would be "new" material to nearly all of us. 
Those with originals to sell would have a larger market of more
motivated fans ("sure, I've got that inexpensive alt.games.frp.tekumel
version, but I want the ORIGINAL, the COLOUR, the FULL-SIZE MAPS!" they
might say).

I would like to see someone do something with a cleaned up version of
the Tekumel Digest, ShadowLands BBS, and this Usenet group.  The amount
of material that has slipped through my fingers is enormous.

What do you all think?  Especially Professor Barker and other Copyright
holders?  If I am out of line, I crave your forgiveness.  If my
worthless ideas can be fashioned into something useful by a mind of
power, may I add my name to the list of interested buyers.

From cheng@pentagon.io.com Sun Apr 23 20:36:44 CDT 1995
Article: 351 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!nobody
From: cheng@pentagon.io.com (David Cheng)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Preserving your Gadarsiyal booklets
Date: 23 Apr 1995 00:49:21 -0500
Organization: Illuminati Online
Lines: 39
Message-ID: <3ncpp1$8n3@pentagon.io.com>
NNTP-Posting-Host: pentagon.io.com
Summary: Use contact paper

There have been several complaints about the durability of the
_Gadarsiyal_ booklets.

Please know that they're _better_ than the RQ booklets that
Avalon Hill puts in their box sets.  Here's a trick to preserve
them very well, if you're willing to do a little arts-and-crafts.

Go to any hardware or kitchenware store.  Buy clear matte contact 
paper.  I'm talking about the plastic sheeting, sticky on one side,
that people use mainly to line shelves.  I have had excellent results
with Rubbermaid brand, "Contact brand self-adhesive plastic, 
Clear color."    It comes in rolls of 3 yards by 18 inches. 
Here in NYC, where prices are always high, one roll goes for
$3.49.  

Cut a piece larger than the cover of the booklet.  The hardest part is
laying the book onto the sticky side without getting bubbles.
I've found that if you do get some bubbles (almost inevitable), 
you can make a tiny pinhole or razor cut, and then push the air out
of the bubble.   Fold the overlap over onto the inside of the
cover.

Advanced craftsmen will remove the staples from the binding 
before applying the plastic.  They will replace them after 
the cover is done, so that the staple goes through the plastic
too.  This really helps the book stay together well, so I
should probably suggest this to be mandatory, and not just
for ambitious devotees.

My RQ books have held up for ten years of heavy use because
of this technique.  And, their original paper covers are 
cheaper and thinner than the Gadarsiyal covers.

Best,
-DC

-- 
* David Cheng          cheng@io.com  <or>  drcheng@sales.stern.nyu.edu
  (212) 472-7752 [before midnite EST]


From slp@uno.edu Mon Apr 24 20:47:49 CDT 1995
Article: 352 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!spool.mu.edu!usenet.eel.ufl.edu!europa.chnt.gtegsc.com!boingo.amil.jhu.edu!blaze.cs.jhu.edu!darwin.sura.net!www.uno.edu!uno.edu!SLP
From: slp@uno.edu
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Re: Tekumel Scripts: Why is ' a consonant?
Date: 21 Apr 1995 19:40:43 GMT
Organization: University of New Orleans
Lines: 27
Message-ID: <3n91nr$3ha@www.uno.edu>
References: <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>
Reply-To: slp@uno.edu
NNTP-Posting-Host: jazz.ucc.uno.edu

In article <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>, rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk (Roger Pearse) writes:
>I've been looking at the Yan Kor script, and noticed that the single quote, 
>', is given as a consonant, both here and in the Tsolyani script.  Does 
>anyone know why, or how this would be used?
>
>--------------------------------------------------------------------
>Roger Pearse                                    rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk
>SoftLab, Networks & Systems                         Tel:01473 644910
>BT Labs                                             Fax:01473 642299
>--------------------------------------------------------------------
>

The ' is used to represent a "glottal stop", which is a "sound" that is
not common in western european languages.  Probably the closest thing
with which you're likely to be familiar is the sound in the "Cockney"
dialect exemplified by the pronounciation of the tt in "bottle" (an
example that Prof. Barker himself has used). Thus, for instance,
Mu'ugalavya (did I spell that right?) is not pronounced like MOOgalavya,
but rather like MOO-OOgalavya.  I think a similar sound in some African 
languages is typically represented by an exclamation point.

HTH

-* Stephen *-
Stephen Posey
SLP@uno.edu
University of New Orleans

Fellow Debtor:

This is going to sound like a con, but in fact IT WORKS!
Five dollars is a small investment in your future.  Forget the lottery
for a week, and give this a try.  It can work for ALL of us.

You can edit this list with a word processor or text editor and then
convert it to a text file.

                                  Good Luck!!

Dear Friend:

My name is Dave Rhodes.  In September 1988 my car was repossessed and the
bill collectors were hounding me like you wouldn't believe.  I was laid
off and my unemployment checks had run out.  The only escape I had from
the pressures of failure was my computer and my modem.  I longed to turn
my advocation into my vocation.

In January 1989 my family and I went on a ten day cruise to the tropics.
I bought a brand new Lincoln Town Car with CASH in February 1989.  I am
currently building a new home on the west coast of Florida, with a private
pool, boat slip, an a beautiful view of the bay from my breakfast room
table and patio.  I will never have to work again.  Today I am RICH!  I
have
earned over $400,000.00 (Four Hundred Thousand Dollars) to date and will
become a millionaire within 4 or 5 months.  Anyone can do the same.  This
money making program works perfectly every time, 100% of the time.  I have
NEVER failed to earn $50,000.00 or more whenever I wanted.  Best of all,
you never have to leave home except to go to your mailbox or post office.

In October 1988, I received a letter in the mail telling me how I could
earn $50,000.00 or more whenever I wanted.  I was naturally very skeptical
and threw the letter on the desk next to my computer.  It's funny though,
when you are desparate, backed into a corner, your mind does crazy things.
I spent a frustrating day looking through the want ads for a job with a
future.  The pickings were sparse at best.  That night I tried to unwind
by booting up my computer and calling several bulletin boards.  I read
several of the messages posted and then glanced at the letter laying next
to the computer.  All at once it became clear to me.  I now had the key to
my dreams.

I realized that with the power of the computer I could expand and enhance
this money making formula into the most unbelievable cash flow generator
that has ever been created.  I substituted the computer bulletin boards in
place of the post office and electronically did by computer what others
were doing by mail.  Now only a few letters are mailed manually.  Most of
the hard work is speedily downloaded to other bulletin boards throughout
the world.  If you believe that someday you deserve that lucky break that
you have waited for all of your life, simply follow the easy instructions
below.  Your dreams WILL come true.


                                                       Sincerely yours,

                                                       Dave Rhodes




     INSTRUCTIONS

Follow these instructions EXACTLY, and in 20 to 60 days you will have
received
well over $50,000.00 cash, all yours.  This program has remained
successful
because of the HONESTY and integrety of the participants.  Please continue
its
success by CAREFULLY ADHERING to the instructions.

Welcome to the world of Mail Order!  This little business is somewhat
different
than most mail order houses.  Your product is not solid and tangible, but
rather a service.  You are in the business of developing Mailing Lists.
Many
large corporations are happy to pay big bucks for quality lists.
(The money made from the mailing lists is secondary to the income which is
 made from people like yourself requesting that they be included in that
list.)


[1]  Immediately mail $1.00 to the first 5 names listed below, starting at
     number 1 through number 5.  SEND CASH ONLY. (Total investment: $5.00)
     Enclose a note with each letter stating: "Please add my name to your
     mailing list".  Include your name and mailing address.
     (This is a legitimate service that you are requesting and you are
paying
     $1.00 for this service.)

[2]  Remove the name that appears as number 1 on the list.  Move the other
     9 names up one position (Number 2 becomes number 1, number 3 becomes
     number 2, and so on).  Place your name, address, and zip code in the
     number 10 position.

[3]  With your name in the number 10 position, upload this ENTIRE file to
     10 (ten) different bulletin boards.  You may post it to the BBS's
     message base or to the file section.  Name it FASTCASH.TXT, and use
the
     file description comments to draw attention to this file and its
great
     potential for all of us.

[4]  Within 60 days you will receive over $50,000.00 in CASH.


Keep a copy of this file for yourself so that you can use it again and
again
whenever you need money.  As soon as you mail out these letters you are
automatically in the mail order business.  People will be sending YOU
$1.00
to be placed on your mailing list.

This list can then be rented to a broker that can be found in your local
yellow pages listings for additional income on a regular basis.  The list
will
become more valuable as it grows in size.

This is a service.  **  IT IS PERFECTLY LEGAL  **

If you have any doubts as to the legality of this service, please refer to
Title 18, Sections 1302 and 1341 of the Postal Lottery Laws.

NOTE:  Make sure that you retain EVERY name and address sent to you,
either
       on computer or hard copy, but do not discard the names and notes
that
       people send to you.  This is PROOF that you are truly providing a
       service, and should the I.R.S. or some other government agency
question
       you, you can provide them with this proof!

Remember, as each post is downloaded and the instructions carefully
followed,
five memebers will be reimbursed for their participation as a List
Developer
with $1.00 each.  Your name will move up the list geometrically so that
when
your name reaches the number 5 position you will be receiving thousands of
dollars in cash.

REMEMBER  -  THIS PROGRAM FAILS ONLY IF YOU ARE NOT HONEST  -  PLEASE!!
             PLEASE BE HONORABLE...IT DOES WORK!  THANK YOU.

The  following letter was written by a participating member in this
program.
**************************************************************************

To those with the COMMON sense to participate in this easy money
opportunity:

     About six months ago I received the enclosed post in letter form.  I
ignored it.  I received about five more of the same letter within the next
two week.I ignored them also.  Of course, I was tempted to follow through
and dreamed of making thousands, but I was convinced it was just another
gimmick and could not possibly work.

I was wrong!  About three weeks later I saw this same letter posted on a
local
bulletin board in Montreal.  I liked the idea of giving it a try with my
computer.  I didn't expect much because I figured, if other people were as
skeptical as I, they would not be too quick to part with $5.00.  But, I
BUY
LOTTERY TICKETS WEEKLY IN MY PROVINCE AND HAVE NOTHING TO SHOW FOR IT BUT
TICKET STUBS!  This week I decided to look at this as my weekly lottery
purchase.  I addressed the envelopes and mailed out $1.00 in each as
directed.
Two weeks went by and I didn't receive anything in the mail.  The fourth
week
rolled around and I couldn't believe what happened!  I can not say that I
received $50,000.00, but it was definitely well over $35,000.00!  For the
first
time in 10 years I got out of debt.  It was great.  Of course, it did not
take
me long to go through my earnings, so I am using this excellent money
opportunity once again.  FOLLOW THE INSTRUCTIONS AND GET READY TO ENJOY!

Please send a copy of this letter along with the enclosed letter so
together
we can convince people who are skeptical that this really does work!


                                                       Good Luck,

                                                       Charles Kust
                                                       St Agathe, Que.
