Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!news.media.mit.edu!grapevine.lcs.mit.edu!olivea!spool.mu.edu!howland.reston.ans.net!pipex!uunet!rice!pound
From: pound@is.rice.edu (Christopher Pound)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Re: Tekumel Scripts: Why is ' a consonant?
Date: 21 Apr 1995 22:52:20 GMT
Organization: Rice University, Houston TX
Lines: 22
Message-ID: <3n9cv4$len@larry.rice.edu>
References: <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>
NNTP-Posting-Host: is.rice.edu

In article <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>,
Roger Pearse <rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk> wrote:
>I've been looking at the Yan Kor script, and noticed that the single quote, 
>', is given as a consonant, both here and in the Tsolyani script.  Does 
>anyone know why, or how this would be used?

I'd guess it's a glottal stop, which is often transcribed with a single
quote ... You actually hear it all the time in English, but we tend to discard
it as a meaningful segment.  Listen to yourself say "'un 'un" like you might
if someone asked you "Have you gotten the new EPT rules yet?"  Or, think of
the cockneyfied pronunciation of "bottle", wherein the "t"s become a sound
you can articulate even if you keep your tongue still.

Or, say "aaaaaah" and then try breaking up all the "a"s like "a'a'a'a'a'a'a".
You'll probably wind up making quite a few glottal stops in the second version.

Improve your German accent by putting glottal stops at the beginning of words
that begin with vowels!  :-)

-- 
Christopher Pound (pound@rice.edu)   |  They think they are Parisians, but
Department of Anthropology, Rice U.  |  they are nothing. -- Pierre Bourdieu

From: tekunu@aol.com (Tekunu)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Re: Tekumel Scripts: Why is ' a consonant?
Date: 22 Apr 1995 07:38:56 -0400
Organization: America Online, Inc. (1-800-827-6364)
Lines: 13
Sender: root@newsbf02.news.aol.com
Message-ID: <3napsg$844@newsbf02.news.aol.com>
References: <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>
Reply-To: tekunu@aol.com (Tekunu)
NNTP-Posting-Host: newsbf02.mail.aol.com

I am not sure.  But having played EPT since the first session in 1975
(with sabbaticals here and there) it is my understanding, ' is a consonant
as the gutteral stop in Cockney English. (Like the Great One!!! Blessings
of the Gods upon him!!! stated in his books).  Bottle for instance becomes
bot'le.  Another example of how the gutteral stop is used as a consonant
can be found among the Khoisan (Southern African languages including
Khoikhoin and the San and used by among others the Kalihari Bushman) where
it is even harsher and comes out as a series of clicking noises.  (More
like the Pe Choi, in fact).  It has a value as a consonant because it is
not a contraction, or a grammatical mark, the sound actually 'takes up
space' and has value.  Please correct me if wrong, Dr. Barker.

Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu

Oh Noble One Whose Quest is One with All!!!!

You played EPT in 1976!!!  Well another old hand is still kicking about. 
Did you play in the University group then?  Are you originally from
Minnesota?  The name does not immediately ring a bell.

As to materials, the new rules are out now.  But you need the Bestiary and
 Volume 1, 1  to generate a character.  The solitaire books are also fun
and give much background to bring someone "up to date" on Tekumel.  Try
going to a used book store and obtain Dr. Barker's two novels: if you
don't already have them.  As to old materials, unfortunately I did all my
Tekumel gaming with Dr. Barker so I have really nothing of my own.

Good luck and thanks for keeping up your interest.

Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu

Mr. Bob:  Tekunu here.

I agree with your positions completely.  This has been discussed before
with the Great One Whose Pen Caresses Paper Like a Perfumed Finger Tickles
the Mistress of the Gods (Dr. Barker).
  The gaming rules are only guidelines to conduct activities on Tekumel
and the gaming rules are not actually the activity itself.  When conflict
arise that require some sort of resolution that cannot be taken care of in
the context of the story line, then rules are required to resolve those
conflicts.  (Usually this is in the realm of combat or a simple
comparative die roll)  Dr. Barker has always said that formost (1) he is a
story teller and (2) the rules are secondary.  I remember many evenings
when I was never required to roll a die, but participated actively in the
story line, having a great time.  I have boiled role playing rules down to
about 8 pages at this time for my own use.

   I agree that more material is necessary.  I am currently working on an
Onchash Chairon module from materials collected during Tekunu
hi'Qolyelmu's epic quest on the Southern Continent for rare flowers to
present to Prince R.  It will include descriptions of about a half dozen
locations in the deep southern continent.  

Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu  (Alan Musielewicz)

Well, it STILL hasn't made it through the distribution channels to Silicon
Valley, but I tell you, I want THREE copies of the map.  One to have and
to hold, and TWO to laminate and or mount together, so I can see the whole
thing at once.

My STRONGEST recommendation is that TOME make the map also available
separately.

ALSO: Although I have the new EPT set on special order, I tried some
other game stores in the San Jose-San Francisco Bay Area, and not one
of them had the new EPT on order.  All insisted that they would NOT be
carrying it, and it would have to be a special order.  This does not
bode well, as this area is one of the most active RPG and gaming markets
in the United States.

Finally, can anyone say whether the errors from the original Swords and
Glory magic system were cleaned up?  In particular, there were MANY Generic
and Temple spells which were Psychic, but their pre-requisite spells
were Ritual (ex: #172 The Attainment of Enlightenment, Psychic, requires
#62 Sagacity, Ritual; there are many others).

Also: in re-examining character generation in Part 1 Adventures in Tekumel,
am I the only one that found buying levels in Sorcery confusing?  In section
7.1 you can buy 1 or 2 levels of Sorcery, but thereafter one seems only
able to buy spells.  Does one even really HAVE levels in Sorcery (or Priest)
or only in sub-skills, or what?

The character generation rules in Adventures in Tekumel are intimidating
and unclear enough that it is no surprise to me that many lost patience
and gave up, which is why Tekumel is on the clearance shelf at the Game
Galleries, and why Gardisyal won't appear on the shelves AT ALL there.

part of the subscription requirements?  

I mean, that way we could *prove* to Professor Barker (May his name be
cheered.  May he be greeted with gladness.  May his footstep be light
and healthful!) and TOME (may their printing presses ring with ever
*increasing* orders for Tekumel products!) that we of "CyberTek(umel)"
are indeed his true followers, and faithful converts to the service of
the Ever-Glorious Petal Throne.

All joking aside, we really need to support *our* hobby.  If an AD&D
2nd Edition Players Handbook, Monsterous Compendium, and Dungeon
Master's Guide sell for about $18-30 a piece (let's assume at least $70
for the set), and we need $75 for the new rules+Bestiary+Character
Generation book, aren't we really talking about the same thing?  And we
can get clarification on a point or two, as needed, from the Professor
or one of his players over the Internet...  Just try getting TSR to
provide that kind of support for, say World of Grayhawk...  :-)

BTW, Mssrs. Bob Alberti and Brett Slocum probably deserve a few kudos
for setting up their cool web pages... regardless of how I feel about
their theology (or they mine!).

An alternative to David's suggested use of contact paper is lamination. You
need to take the books apart and remove the covers. Take these (along with 
the new maps) to your local Kinko's or other copy shop and have them 
laminated. Trim the lamination and put the books back together. Many shops
offer a choice or rigid or soft laminate.

Rob

	As far as the new map goes:  it's beautiful, but without a 
hex-grid, it's a little trickier defining exactly where the adventurers 
might be at any one time.  The original EPT and the later Gamescience 
maps, with their lamination, allowed you to use an overhead projection 
pen to mark where the players last stopped.  I don't know if I'd want to 
do that with the new map; it looks less "sturdy" to me.
	The new map's scale of 10 Tsan to every 7 millimeters is 
interesting, but for those of us who can't do math in their heads (like 
me), it's going to be a little tricky.  "Let's see, your group has gone on a 
tube car and covered about 2,354 millimeters.  Hmmmmm.  That's, uh.....  
23 divided by 7, carry the remainder......   Where's a calculator?"  ;)
	Seriously, folks:  the new map is very nice and looks like a real 
map, unlike the ones in the past.  Unfortunately, I won't be laying the 
new map down where something can be spilled on it, and I'll always have 
to keep a ruler or some improvised gauge to determine distances.  Other 
than those two concerns, I'll treasure this map.  After all, since I've 
got the earlier maps, I can use them instead and leave the new one safely 
inside its game box.

				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas

Organization: inlink
Lines: 47
Message-ID: <Pine.BSD/.3.91.950421125001.28374D-100000@vulcan.inlink.com>
References: <3muaq0$q7f@giga.bga.com> <3n1fsc$dtt@pentagon.io.com> <wdf-1904952244290001@192.0.2.1>
NNTP-Posting-Host: vulcan.inlink.com
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII
In-Reply-To: <wdf-1904952244290001@192.0.2.1> 

	I agree that people new to Tekumel are going to have a rough time 
of it with just Gardasiyal.  Without even a minimal sketch of Tekumel, 
the potential new GM is going to be puzzled by these rules.  After all, 
he'll have to at least buy the Tekumel Source books (and won't he be 
angry when he realizes that he's only got two-thirds of the background 
info!), even so he can figure out what all the fuss is about this strange 
world.
	Most potential GM's have used some game system in the past, and 
will probably be miffed at not having even a quick-generation system for 
creating NPC's (the archetypes will be used up by his players).  The 
monster stats will do in the early going, and this poses no real problem, 
as far as I see.  The encounter charts limit which monsters show up 
where and when.
	So the main problem I see is a GM who's never heard of Tekumel 
will have a tough time figuring out the background from the very scanty 
information provided in Gardasiyal, will end up sinking another $24 just 
to get the campaign started!  This will discourage quite a few people who 
can get an entire campaign in one book/box, not just not just the final 
five pieces of the puzzle that is Tekumel.
	For example, Castle Falkenstein, by R. Talsorian Games, is 224 
pages long and  comes in either hardback or softback format.  Over 
one-half of it is devoted to background information, maps and so on, 
while the other portion covers the game rules.  It has a table of 
contents and an index, too, making looking something up far easier.  And 
do you know how much this complete and ready-to-go game, set in a 
fantastic faerie-filled Victorian Europe, sells for?  $32 for the 
hardback and $27 for the softback!
	Now, if I were looking for an exotic setting to run an RPG in, 
and had never before heard of Tekumel, but still wanted to check both 
out, I'd spend my copious money (this *is* hypothetical!) to buy both 
sets of rules:  Gardasiyal and Castle Falkenstein.  After about two or 
three hours' comparison, I'd sell off the Tekumel stuff and begin working 
on setting up a C.F. campaign right away!


				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas

myself.  They need a little tinkering (the Experience rules, 
especially!), but overall, with all the solo books and previous 
incarnations of Tekumel rules at my disposal, I can run a game.

system at all to play!  I wish I had your spare time to do all the work 
that would make that possible for me to do as well.  However, since I'm 
going to have to piece together a complete rules system, it's going to be 
at least another month before I can start my campaign up again.
	Not to mention the fact that since I haven't run a Tekumel game 
in over 11 years, it's going to be darn hard to find players.  Everybody 
I know is just as busy as I am, so I'll have to go find a new group of 
gamers to play the game.  Hmmm.  Another month's delay.

In article <3n9du6$rue@newsbf02.news.aol.com>,
LORD SARKU <lordsarku@aol.com> wrote:
>I was in contact with the good folk at TOME today and was informed that a
>few box sets of Gardasiyal were shipped without a small 'Introduction to
>Gardasiyal' booklet. 
>
>If you are one of those unfortunates, it is available FREE of charge just
>by writing to TOME and alerting them of the oversight.

I just received mine in the mail today.  I believe everyone who pre-ordered
and didn't get the Intro, will probably get it by mail in the next week 
or so.

I must say that this Intro goes a long way toward addressing some concerns
with the set.  Though it is only 4 pages long, it contains the proviso
about AoT, Part one and the Bestiary, plus about 3 pages of historical
intro to Tekumel, including some facts I was not aware of (the Pe Choi
gave humans the Three-Light drive). It is unfortunate that the box back
has the erroneous statement 'You now hold a complete, complex, alien
and thoroughly enjoyable world' (my quibble is with 'complete world').
But for that statement (and the lack of a statement on the box about needing the 
other books) this would be a reasonably packaged game. Not perfect min
you, but what is these days.

Anyway, I encourage everyone to try it out.  After all, this is the
only game in print that you can get all the wonderful spells for
Tekumel (always my favorite part of S&G).

Enjoy!

In <3nari5$89k@newsbf02.news.aol.com>, tekunu@aol.com (Tekunu)  wrote:
> 
>   The gaming rules are only guidelines...the rules are secondary...

Yes, but when someone buys a GAME, they evaluate it primarily by the RULES.
(GAME = RULES).  How many people bought Adventures in Tekumel, and were
turned off by the rules?  How many weren't turned off immediately, but
gave up buying endless solitaire games while waiting for the rules?
How many potential referees turned their attention to other games because
no rules were forthcoming, and the few examples they saw were not up to
modern standards for RPGS.

Tekumel should have been marketted as a series of WORLD BOOKS, and ignored
rules almost entirely (the only exception really being Magic).  EPT has
never been a RULE set, but a WORLD set, and should have been presented as
such.

TOME could hardly have done a worse job in marketting the materials:

1992:	Adventures in Tekumel: a complex system of character generation
	for a game that will not be available for THREE YEARS.
	The Tekumel Bestiary: a collection of statistics for creatures
	for a role playing game whose rules will not be available for
	THREE YEARS.
1992-
1995:	Various solitaire adventures designed to develop characters for
	a game system that is NOT AVAILABLE.  Those who do develop
	characters CANNOT find a referee, because the rules are NOT
	AVAILABLE, and won't be for years.

1995:	After 3 years of diminishing sales of SUPPLEMENTARY products,
	the game these materials are supposed to supplement is finally
	published.  At this point, stores no longer carry the line, and
	it must be special ordered.  To add insult to injury, TOME offers
	a 25% discount for direct orders from the manufacturer, which
	bypasses the DISTRIBUTION chain, virtually assuring that future
	editions will not be available in stores.
	
	Further, the game is incomplete, lacking character generation,
	and requires supplements no longer available on store shelves.
	
According to my local game store, TOME is soliciting orders for three
more supplements, and I will order these, but I will be surprised if
TOME actually publishes all three.

Organization: Rice University, Houston TX
Lines: 22
Message-ID: <3n9cv4$len@larry.rice.edu>
References: <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>
NNTP-Posting-Host: is.rice.edu

In article <3n8fel$6on@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>,
Roger Pearse <rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk> wrote:
>I've been looking at the Yan Kor script, and noticed that the single quote, 
>', is given as a consonant, both here and in the Tsolyani script.  Does 
>anyone know why, or how this would be used?

I'd guess it's a glottal stop, which is often transcribed with a single
quote ... You actually hear it all the time in English, but we tend to discard
it as a meaningful segment.  Listen to yourself say "'un 'un" like you might
if someone asked you "Have you gotten the new EPT rules yet?"  Or, think of
the cockneyfied pronunciation of "bottle", wherein the "t"s become a sound
you can articulate even if you keep your tongue still.

Or, say "aaaaaah" and then try breaking up all the "a"s like "a'a'a'a'a'a'a".
You'll probably wind up making quite a few glottal stops in the second version.

Improve your German accent by putting glottal stops at the beginning of words
that begin with vowels!  :-)

-- 
Christopher Pound (pound@rice.edu)   |  They think they are Parisians, but
Department of Anthropology, Rice U.  |  they are nothing. -- Pierre Bourdieu

Setnaffa, an excellent source for news and adventures is the fanzine
The Eye of All-Seeing Wonder, available for $6 (cash, I believe, even
though mailing cash out of the country is illegal) from
   Steve Foster, 26 Western Lane, Balham, London  SW12 8JS  United Kingdom
 
Not just to toot my own horn, but Issue #4 (the current issue) has my
adventure "Behind Enemy Lines", complete with characters.  It uses Dave
Morris's excellent Tirikelu rules system, but I have these nine characters
converted over to Gardasiyal rules--four of them are senior (experienced)
types, and five are beginners.  Each issue had at least one adventure,
and many of them include characters.  If you need adventures, there are
plenty of hooks to get you started--many adventures are excellent beginnings
to new campaigns, and at $6 an issue, it's much cheaper than most adventures.
You'll like the rest of the magazine, too.

From rdushay@delphi.com Sat Apr 29 10:19:06 CDT 1995
Article: 374 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!satisfied.apocalypse.org!news2.near.net!news.delphi.com!usenet
From: Robert Dushay <rdushay@delphi.com>
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Review of the rules in action
Date: Sun, 23 Apr 95 21:59:51 -0500
Organization: Delphi (info@delphi.com email, 800-695-4005 voice)
Lines: 63
Message-ID: <ZS+d5Lf.rdushay@delphi.com>
NNTP-Posting-Host: bos1e.delphi.com

I just finished gaming using the new rules this past weekend.  My
experience was generally positive, although the players (experienced
roleplayers all) had some complaints.  First, the good.
 
1. Combat works just fine.  It's fast, smooth, satisfactory, and playable.
William Faulkner complained that there are too many modifiers--maybe, but
with a little management, they aren't a problem.  If you follow the
examples of the character sheet in the Archetypes booklet, you have your
players list their initiative and to hit mods for each weapon on their
character sheet.  Then, all you eseentially have to keep track of is
whether they were wounded.
   I confess to also having a secret weapon for these things: I retype all
key tables into my wordprocessor, and print out a referee cheat sheet that
has all relevant modifiers on one page, along with the relevant tables.
I have one page for initiative, another for to-hit rolls, and another for
damage.  It works well for me.
 
2. The skill rolls and all the rest of the rules were fine.  They were
transparent enough so that I could focus on the action and telling the story,
and they were fast enough that I could whip them out and roll when I felt
I needed a random element.  As usual in my better Tekumel games, the focus
was on the story and the player interaction; the rules worked to support
that very well.
 
Complaints.  My players were mainly ticked off that the d100 character
generation system, and the HBS attack system meant that a player who rolled
lucky at the very beginning had an enormous, and insurmountable advantage
over the rest of the party.  It's the same sort of grousing I've heard in
AD&D where two fighters have 18/90+ strengths--it tends to devalue the rest
of the warriors.  Maybe my players were just lucky, but we did have some
huge differences in ability for ostensibly equal characters.
 
The other big stink was over spell-casting.  The sorcerers felt that at
their tender levels, they had essentially one chance to get a spell off
(35% chance for successful casting, and their psychic power was enough for
only three casts), and it took too long to recover points.  This could be
adjusted (one suggestion was that failed spells didn't cost the same as
a successful one).
 
A lesser complaint was that the skill system was confusing: they felt a
maximum of 5 skill levels in languages, while 30 for everything else made
no sense, and they had trouble comparing their skills to others.  As
referee, I had no such confusion, but the players have to be happy, too.
 
I don't think Gardasiyal is state of the art, but I'm not sure what state
of the art is.  The most popular system around is AD&D, 2nd edition, and
I wouldn't consider that state of the art, either.  Gardasiyal works, it
permits me to simulate the world well enough, and it provides the key
information we've been missing for years: monster stats congruent with
player stats, how Eyes work in relation to spell-casting, etc.  I'm heart-
broken over the way this game has been packaged and marketed (broken up
into pieces, with no clear guidance for players as to what to buy and
which units are needed for what), but there's enough to make a go of it,
and the system is far more workable than Swords and Glory was.  I hope to
continue to support these rules--even if my regular group won't use them,
I'll still try to run games at conventions using them--and I hope that Tekumel
continues as a living product.
 
Anybody else actually /playing/ these rules?
 
--Bob Dushay
Dritlan, The Legion of Obscure Books
1st Imperial Heavy Scholars


From rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk Sat Apr 29 10:19:07 CDT 1995
Article: 375 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!cs.utexas.edu!swrinde!pipex!bt!usenet
From: rpearse@srd.bt.co.uk (Roger Pearse)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: GARDASIYAL: Impressions
Date: 24 Apr 1995 08:18:23 GMT
Organization: BT plc
Lines: 71
Message-ID: <3nfmsf$n75@pheidippides.axion.bt.co.uk>
NNTP-Posting-Host: horizon.srd.bt.co.uk
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=US-ASCII
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
X-Newsreader: WinVN 0.99.2

Well, I've just received my copy of this, and wondered a bit what all the 
fuss was about.  Points that struck me:

- Very nice box.  It has oodles of shelf appeal, and rather reminded me of 
the old RuneQuest supplements.  Should help it sell alright.

- I was glad to see the dice.  I think I'd have felt cheated if I bought a 
game and there were no dice in it.

- Lovely maps: easily the nicest ever produced for EPT.  For the first time 
I worked out where the legions of Eselne and Mirusiya were moving in the 
original attack on Yan Kor.  I liked the 'papyrus' borders, and the glyphs 
on them.  Anyone know what they stand for?

- I saw the reference to the Temple book, Mituminyal, appearing in 1996.  I 
devoutly hope it will.

- The 3 booklets will also be available seperately: a great idea!  Encourage 
your players to buy the players guide.

- The covers of the 3 booklets had a very RQ'ish sort of feel, and were very 
good.  These are easily the best looking EPT rules we've ever had.

- I was missing the intro booklet, so I felt vol 1 started rather suddenly. 
I think a sticker on the box saying that Growing Up in Tekumel is a 
pre-requisite should be printed.  I can see why they didn't want to repeat 
all that, but a cover sticker would have deflected much criticism.

- This is the first complete role-playing system published for tekumel since 
EPT.  It's very important for that reason: it is now *possible* to play 
Tekumel out of the box.  I understood the rules clearly enough, and was very
glad to get it.  I expect 2nd hand sales of S&G II will drop rather acutely!

- The paper is thinner than that used for the solo books, but I don't see 
there's anything wrong with it.  The typesetting is good, apart from the 
strange decision to allow ragged right, rather than justified.  I think the 
layout of the solo books was better, but this is nit-picking.  There wasn't 
anything wrong with them.

- I very much liked the pre-generated characters.  This was a very sensible 
move, and helped illustrate the whole process of character generation.

- The magic system was clearly explained, and it was new to me.  Its hould 
work well, and give a distinctive tekumelani feel to the game.

- My overall impression is that this is Swords & Glory 2nd Edition, cut 
down,
better laid out, and easier to follow.  This even extends to a snippet of 
S&G appearing (with section references!  Did no one proof read it?) on page 
14 at the top.

- A starting scenario would have been nice.  

So how do I feel overall?  Very positive.  I feel that a lot of the 
criticism
is because people didn't want rules, they wanted another sourcebook.  Now I
can understand that - I'd like more Tekumel info too - but we did badly need
a set of rules.  Yes there are nitpicks about some of the production - but
its still the best produced set of rules Tekumel has ever had.  I think all
of us could think of extra things we'd like in it: but remember new players
are expected to start with the solo books, not with a big boxed set.  I know
it isn't all that cheap, but then what do you expect from a small company?

So I'd like to thank all those who produced it, and hope for more.

BT Labs                                             Fax:01473 642299

There was some talk about how to type right to left.  I found a utility
which allows the entry of text this way, and have attached it.  It was part
of a shareware distribution of greek and hebrew fonts, sfonts10.zip.  I've
cut it down to just the r2l utility.  Instructions are included.  It works 
with the Tsolyani font.

Anton:

Yes indeed the frustrations you have expressed are those of many members
of the gaming community attempting to play Tekumel.  The problem is that
those of us who have had an opportunity to play with Dr. Barker for a
number of years  tend to forget how frustrating it is for those who do not
have that opportunity.  Within our heads (and Dr. Barker's) are an
incredible wealth of details about Tekumel that would be almost impossible
to sort through, and relate.  Some of us have kept regular journals of our
adventures, to mark in details of Tekumel as we explore.  My own notes
would fill probably a half dozen modules.  They should be related to
others to enjoy.
  It is just because of that wealth of knowledge that rules become less
necessary.  When I play Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu.  I am Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu of
the Golden Sunburst Clan.  I know what my fief looks like.  I know my
retainors.  I see these things in my mind's eye.  I  don't need to roll
much because I know my limitations .  It is not so much that rules are
unnecessary as that there is little need to roll under conditions where
role playing is more of a vision or a panorama than a game.  

Alan

In article <3ncrt1$mcd@donald.cc.utexas.edu>,
Robert Smith <resmith@donald.cc.utexas.edu> wrote:
>An alternative to David's suggested use of contact paper is lamination. You
>need to take the books apart and remove the covers. Take these (along with 
>the new maps) to your local Kinko's or other copy shop and have them 
>laminated. Trim the lamination and put the books back together. Many shops
>offer a choice or rigid or soft laminate.


Also, this usually doesn't yellow as fast as the contact paper, it protects 
both the inside and outside, and if the job is screwed up, you have someone 
besides yourself to blame.

Oh Noble One Whose Quest is One with All!!!!

You played EPT in 1976!!!  Well another old hand is still kicking about. 
Did you play in the University group then?  Are you originally from
Minnesota?  The name does not immediately ring a bell.

As to materials, the new rules are out now.  But you need the Bestiary and
 Volume 1, 1  to generate a character.  The solitaire books are also fun
and give much background to bring someone "up to date" on Tekumel.  Try
going to a used book store and obtain Dr. Barker's two novels: if you
don't already have them.  As to old materials, unfortunately I did all my
Tekumel gaming with Dr. Barker so I have really nothing of my own.

Good luck and thanks for keeping up your interest.

Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu

Mr. Bob:  Tekunu here.

I agree with your positions completely.  This has been discussed before
with the Great One Whose Pen Caresses Paper Like a Perfumed Finger Tickles
the Mistress of the Gods (Dr. Barker).
  The gaming rules are only guidelines to conduct activities on Tekumel
and the gaming rules are not actually the activity itself.  When conflict
arise that require some sort of resolution that cannot be taken care of in
the context of the story line, then rules are required to resolve those
conflicts.  (Usually this is in the realm of combat or a simple
comparative die roll)  Dr. Barker has always said that formost (1) he is a
story teller and (2) the rules are secondary.  I remember many evenings
when I was never required to roll a die, but participated actively in the
story line, having a great time.  I have boiled role playing rules down to
about 8 pages at this time for my own use.

   I agree that more material is necessary.  I am currently working on an
Onchash Chairon module from materials collected during Tekunu
hi'Qolyelmu's epic quest on the Southern Continent for rare flowers to
present to Prince R.  It will include descriptions of about a half dozen
locations in the deep southern continent.  

Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu  (Alan Musielewicz)

In <RQ69Zdd.rdushay@delphi.com> Robert Dushay <rdushay@delphi.com> writes: 
>
>An excellent idea that suffers from one major obstacle: somebody has to
>actually do the legwork.  Setnaffa, I believe the ball is in your court.
>You have the idea, and you have the motivation.  Perhaps you could track
>down the holders of these corights, pitch your idea to them, and find
>out what it would cost?
> 
>--Bob Dushay
>Dritlan, the Legion of Obscure Books

Now, if Professor Barker will give me permission to proceed, I will
gladly take on the "legwork", the scanning/typing/gathering work, and
whatever assembling that it takes.  I will submit all materials to him
and/or his representative for approval before releasing/publishing it. 
And I will submit to the censure of this newsgroup (virtual
impalement?) if I do not abide by Professor Barker's wishes.

My current plan is to collect everything and "reorg" it with a table of
contents and maybe an index.  I have the TSR EPT, Dragon #4, The Best
of the Tekumel Journals Vol.1, and the Space Gamer S&G Special Issue
(#71?).  I would like to get an approved way to collect all of the
other materials without too much trouble (or money, which I don't have
in unlimited supplies, either).

Please, all of you, look at the materials you have and send me the
names of authors other than the Professor.  Have them email me or if
you get their address to me, I'll contact them.  I will also contact
the various magazines (Dragon, Space Gamer, etc.) and try to get their
permissions.  Does anyone have current addresses for Lou Zocchi? 
Different Worlds (for example, did they turn into Sleuth Publications)?
 Does TOME have all the rights for previously published stuff?  Send
email answers to setnaffa@ix.netcom.com; send snailmail to John T.
Bailey, 1901 W Spring Creek #507, Plano, TX 75023-4220.  Anything sent
in for archiving will be returned unopened unless previously approved
by the Professor.  The last thing we need is to irritate him or TOME. 
We want to enhance interest in Tekumel, not discourage further
investment.

Here is what I have determined to be available, excluding the books
TOME is actually publishing...

>Yes indeed the frustrations you have expressed are those of many
members
>of the gaming community attempting to play Tekumel.  The problem is
that
>those of us who have had an opportunity to play with Dr. Barker for a
>number of years  tend to forget how frustrating it is for those who do
not
>have that opportunity.  Within our heads (and Dr. Barker's) are an
>incredible wealth of details about Tekumel that would be almost
impossible
>to sort through, and relate.  Some of us have kept regular journals of
our
>adventures, to mark in details of Tekumel as we explore.  My own notes
>would fill probably a half dozen modules.  They should be related to
>others to enjoy.

so enough with the "attitude" and publish the "Fief of the Golden
Sunburst Clan" already...  :-)

What we need is men and women to share the game in a way that is
*meaningful* to others who have not shared the richness of the environs
of Tsolyanu.  I, for one, have not played for over 18 years.  But over
the last few months, I have bought almost $200.00 worth of stuff (to my
wife's disgust and amazement-- after all, it's so...old) and will buy
the new rules when I can again muster $44.00+s&h (no stores in Dallas
seem to carry it, yet!).  Be assured, I *will* play again.  Even if it
requires tricking my D&D playing friends into another world for a few
sessions.  >:->

Let's see some of those 20 years of Professor Barker's games described
by the players in great detail.  I am certain that there would even be
a certain group of players who would expend their hard-earned Kaitars
for a good story, module, or even the plans of an underground temple or
two...  (hint, hint, nudge, stomp!)  8-D

On the other hand, if you keep the game's highr moments to yourselves,
the game will die again.  And then there will be no one to revivify it.
 :-(

We're getting our second wind, and NOW is the time to JUMP!!!!

From: gauntlet@bga.com (Jeff)

Subject: Re: Wading into battle
Date: 26 Apr 1995 15:22:52 GMT
Organization: Real/Time Communications - Bob Gustwick and Associates
Lines: 41
Message-ID: <3nlogc$sas@giga.bga.com>
References: <766231d4118368t202@anton.infoserv.com> <3nh533$mcj@newsbf02.news.aol.com>
NNTP-Posting-Host: ghostwheel.bga.com
X-Newsreader: TIN [version 1.2 PL2]

Tekunu (tekunu@aol.com) wrote:

: Yes indeed the frustrations you have expressed are those of many members
: of the gaming community attempting to play Tekumel.  The problem is that
: those of us who have had an opportunity to play with Dr. Barker for a
: number of years  tend to forget how frustrating it is for those who do not
: have that opportunity.  Within our heads (and Dr. Barker's) are an
: incredible wealth of details about Tekumel that would be almost impossible
: to sort through, and relate.  Some of us have kept regular journals of our
: adventures, to mark in details of Tekumel as we explore.  My own notes
: would fill probably a half dozen modules.  They should be related to
: others to enjoy.
:   It is just because of that wealth of knowledge that rules become less
: necessary.  When I play Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu.  I am Tekunu hi'Qolyelmu of
: the Golden Sunburst Clan.  I know what my fief looks like.  I know my
: retainors.  I see these things in my mind's eye.  I  don't need to roll
: much because I know my limitations .  It is not so much that rules are
: unnecessary as that there is little need to roll under conditions where
: role playing is more of a vision or a panorama than a game.  

The frustration of those of us whose playstyle relies more on game 
mechanics than yours must also be recognized.  It doesn't matter to us 
whether or not the professor's group plays without dice or rules; many of 
*us* do, and it annoys us to see substandard game mechanics attached to a 
world we like so much.  It's far easier for those of you who *don't* use 
dice to simply ignore the game mechanics than for those of us who use 
dice to play with a set of rules that are not up to par.

That being said, I actually don't find the rules in Gardasiyal to be that 
bad.  What I do kind of mind is the Professor's stated objection to 
running Tekumel under any *other* set of rules.  I intend to replace the 
Gardasiyal mechanics with my own (not because the Gardasiyal rules are so 
bad, but because my group and I are more comfortable with another system) 
while using Gardasiyal as the template for world-relevant things like 
clan, lineage, education, professional rank advancement, and so on.

WWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWWW

        gauntlet@bga.com        Sic Gorgiamus Subjectatus Allos Nunc

Professor Barker:  If you do not want me to continue, would you or Bob
Alberti please contact me?  Otherwise, I will consider that I have your
implicit permission.

********************************************************************

If you "more experienced" players will take the time to write to me
(email, snailmail, fax, whatever) I'll see that your past game
experiences get published somewhere--current fanzine(s) or TOME or me.

You "less experienced" players:  Let's see a "show of hands" on this. 
Send email to "setnaffa@ix.netcom.com"" stating you would be interested
in a writeup of someone else's gaming experiences.  If not enough
people are interested, I'll just sit down and shut up.  If I get enough
response, I'll do whatever it takes to get the materials available to
all.

********************************************************************

Let's create a mailing list to pass around to various gaming businesses
(like TOME, PHD, and so on) stating that we are interested in Tekumel
related stuff.  I don't mean a "listserv", but a real-life marketing
tool.  In this way we could show the businesses that we were a viable
market.  We would be saving them money by doing their market research
for them.  And we would be able to organize ourselves a little better.

Send me an email stating you wish to be added to the list.  Perhaps
Brett or Bob could eventually allocate space on one of their webpages
to advertise for us, but for now, I'm stepping up to the plate and just
swinging.

*******************************************************************

If you want any previously published stuff to be included in the
materials I will be releasing, please go ahead and send it now. 
However, I will be doing my utmost to contact any and all interested
parties to get a release of some sort.  

********************************************************************

Will someone with a good contact at TOME email me concerning what
previously published materials are owned by TOME?  Also, I would like
to find a way to limit my output to people who have purchased the new
rules--what is the best way to handle that?

********************************************************************

Finally, whatever happened to Tekumel Games?  As far as my records
indicate, they went to Rio with all of the money.  Do they have any
stake in this game?  Did TOME get their rights?

********************************************************************

Thanks to everyone who has responded so far  :-D

From wybesse@aol.com Sat Apr 29 10:19:28 CDT 1995

Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!usc!howland.reston.ans.net!newsjunkie.ans.net!newstf01.news.aol.com!newsbf02.news.aol.com!not-for-mail
From: wybesse@aol.com (Wybesse)
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Re: Religions And Frp
Date: 26 Apr 1995 22:51:46 -0400
Organization: America Online, Inc. (1-800-827-6364)
Lines: 28
Sender: root@newsbf02.news.aol.com
Message-ID: <3nn0s2$2dn@newsbf02.news.aol.com>
References: <3mmd5m$47c@cedar.mr.net>
Reply-To: wybesse@aol.com (Wybesse)
NNTP-Posting-Host: newsbf02.mail.aol.com

>Gods are insane precisely because their goals and motives are not
>bound to human strictures.  A god might say with perfect certainty,
>"The reason that suffering exists is because those yellow flowers are
>discordant and Tuesday."  For all practical human purposes, that god
>is insane, despite the fact that as a god, they are undoubtedy correct.

Ook!  Signor Alberti, let me suggest that you are suffering from what the
ancient Greeks were wont to call hubris.  Gods don't make sense to humans,
so Gods are "insane"?  An interesting, but to my mind unconventional use
of the word.

>[Gods] could no more meanin[g]fully interact with me than I could with a
>blood cell.  If a god cannot interact with the universe, than Occam's
>razor suggests that gods aren't there at all.

A plentitude of fascinating observations.  (a) What makes you think you
can't interact with a blood cell?  You interact with millions of them
every day. (b) What is the justification for assuming that
gods/God:you::you:(apparently)unconscious matter? (c) you are misapplying
the (overhyped) postulate of William of Occam ("entia non sunt
multiplicanda praeter necessitatem"); how does the inability (even given
this dubious assertion) to interact affect one's "necessity"?

Occam is a bit of a thin reed anyway; there are far too many things in the
real world (let alone the imagination) that are far more complex than they
"need" to be.

No offense intended; I just relish a good discussion.  :-)

From rkurgas@vulcan.inlink.com Sun Apr 30 11:05:25 CDT 1995
Article: 412 of alt.games.frp.tekumel
Path: news.io.com!news.tamu.edu!bloom-beacon.mit.edu!news.starnet.net!wupost!news.inlink.com!vulcan.inlink.com!rkurgas
From: Rick Kurgas <rkurgas@vulcan.inlink.com>
Newsgroups: alt.games.frp.tekumel
Subject: Parrying Rules
Date: Thu, 27 Apr 1995 03:36:31 -0500
Organization: inlink
Lines: 64
Message-ID: <Pine.BSD/.3.91.950427031014.19453B-100000@vulcan.inlink.com>
NNTP-Posting-Host: vulcan.inlink.com
Mime-Version: 1.0
Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; charset=US-ASCII

	I thought it'd be nice to have rules so a character can parry.  
Under the present rules, you'd be insane not to have a half-dozen shields 
on hand to hopefully catch some of the (massive) damage meant for you.  
They also discourages "Florentine" fighting, since you can't use either 
weapon to parry and set up a counter-reposte.  You just take the damage 
on your never-gets-damaged armor and lump the damage that penetrates.
	Well, anyway, here they are:

	Parry Rules
	-----------

	Types of Parrying Tools
	-----------------------
	U:  Bows and Light, Improvised (a shinbone, for example)
	V:  Heavy, Improvised (a wooden chair, for example)
	W:  Small, One-Handed Weapons (a dagger, for example)
	X:  Pike, Quarterstaff, Spear, Javelin or Polearm
	Y:  Long One-Handed Weapons (a sword, for example)
	Z:  Two-Handed Weapons (a Flamberge, for example)

	Parry Chart
	-----------
	D10 Score to Avoid Damage		Weapon Hit Points
	-------------------------		-----------------
	U:  1 (only)					5
	V:  1-2						10
	W:  1-3						15
	X:  1-4						20
	Y:  1-4						25
	Z:  1-5						30

	Add 1 for every 10 Levels		If weapon is steel, add 10
	in appropriate weapon skill		If weapon is enchanted,
	Steel Weapons add 1			add 20
	Enchanted Weapons add 2

	As you can see by these charts, they allow some chance of 
parrying opponent's blows.  Unless you're fighting Florentine, however, 
you forfeit your attack in order to parry.  When you are fighting 
Florentine, you may attack with one weapon and parry with the other, or 
attack with both, OR parry with both.
	The maximum number possible is if you're level 30 in a 2-handed 
weapon that's enchanted, which is 1-9.  You can still blow it by rolling 
a 10.  Also, the weapon's hit points can be increased, but the maximum 
comes out to be equal to an enchanted shield.  That means most warriors 
will still prefer a shield, but better skilled and better equipped 
warriors have options.  Not to mention non-warriors will have *something* 
with which to ward off damage, at least sometimes.
	Let me know what you think of this idea.  I'm still working on a 
hit-point system for the armor.  If you're going to represent damage to 
some of your equipment, you should represent it all!

				Sincerely,

				Rick Kurgas
